---
collectionId: "9ktkng9a95n6199"
collectionName: "pages"
content: "<p>The <strong>Boston Celtics</strong> (<span class=\"rt-commentedText nowrap\"><span class=\"IPA nopopups noexcerpt\" lang=\"en-fonipa\"><a title=\"Help:IPA/English\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/English\">/<span style=\"border-bottom: 1px dotted;\"><span title=\"/ˈ/: primary stress follows\">ˈ</span><span title=\"'s' in 'sigh'\">s</span><span title=\"/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'\">ɛ</span><span title=\"'l' in 'lie'\">l</span><span title=\"'t' in 'tie'\">t</span><span title=\"/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'\">ɪ</span><span title=\"'k' in 'kind'\">k</span><span title=\"'s' in 'sigh'\">s</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a title=\"Help:Pronunciation respelling key\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key\"><em title=\"English pronunciation respelling\"><span style=\"font-size: 90%;\">SEL</span>-tiks</em></a>) are an American professional <a title=\"Basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball\">basketball</a> team based in <a title=\"Boston\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston\">Boston</a>. The Celtics compete in the <a title=\"National Basketball Association\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association\">National Basketball Association</a> (NBA) as a member of the league's <a title=\"Eastern Conference (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Conference_(NBA)\">Eastern Conference</a> <a title=\"Atlantic Division (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Division_(NBA)\">Atlantic Division</a>. Founded in 1946 as one of the league's original eight teams, the Celtics play their home games at <a title=\"TD Garden\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TD_Garden\">TD Garden</a>, which is also the home of the <a title=\"National Hockey League\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Hockey_League\">National Hockey League</a>'s <a title=\"Boston Bruins\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Bruins\">Boston Bruins</a>. The Celtics are one of the most successful teams in NBA history. The franchise's 17 NBA championships are the joint most of any team, alongside the <a title=\"Los Angeles Lakers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers\">Los Angeles Lakers</a>. The Celtics currently hold the record for the <a title=\"List of all-time NBA win&ndash;loss records\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_all-time_NBA_win%E2%80%93loss_records\">most recorded wins</a> of any NBA team.<sup id=\"cite_ref-8\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-8\">[8]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-9\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-9\">[9]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Celtics have <a title=\"Celtics&ndash;Lakers rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtics%E2%80%93Lakers_rivalry\">a notable rivalry</a> with the Los Angeles Lakers, which was heavily highlighted throughout the 1960s and 1980s. During the two teams' many match-ups in the 1980s, the Celtics' star, <a title=\"Larry Bird\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_Bird\">Larry Bird</a>, and the Lakers' star, <a title=\"Magic Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_Johnson\">Magic Johnson</a>, had an ongoing feud. The franchise has played the Lakers a record 12 times in the <a title=\"NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a> (including recent appearances in <a title=\"2008 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_NBA_Finals\">2008</a> and <a title=\"2010 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_NBA_Finals\">2010</a>), of which the Celtics have won nine.<sup id=\"cite_ref-10\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-10\">[10]</a></sup> Four Celtics players (<a title=\"Bob Cousy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Cousy\">Bob Cousy</a>, <a title=\"Bill Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Russell\">Bill Russell</a>, <a title=\"Dave Cowens\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Cowens\">Dave Cowens</a> and Larry Bird) have won the <a title=\"NBA Most Valuable Player Award\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Most_Valuable_Player_Award\">NBA Most Valuable Player Award</a> for an NBA record total of 10 MVP awards.<sup id=\"cite_ref-11\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-11\">[11]</a></sup> Both the nickname \"Celtics\" and their mascot \"Lucky the Leprechaun\" are a nod to <a title=\"History of Irish Americans in Boston\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Irish_Americans_in_Boston\">Boston's historically large Irish population</a>, and also to the <a title=\"Original Celtics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Original_Celtics\">Original Celtics</a>, a marquee team prior to the NBA.<sup id=\"cite_ref-12\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-12\">[12]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Celtics' rise to dominance began in the late 1950s, after the team, led by coach <a title=\"Red Auerbach\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Auerbach\">Red Auerbach</a>, acquired <a title=\"Center (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_(basketball)\">center</a> Bill Russell, who would become the cornerstone of the Celtics dynasty, in a draft-day trade in 1956. Led by Russell and <a title=\"Point guard\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Point_guard\">point guard</a> Bob Cousy, the Celtics won their first NBA championship in 1957. Russell, along with a talented supporting cast of future <a title=\"Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame\">Hall of Famers</a> including <a title=\"John Havlicek\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Havlicek\">John Havlicek</a>, <a title=\"Tom Heinsohn\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Heinsohn\">Tom Heinsohn</a>, <a title=\"K. C. Jones\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K._C._Jones\">K. C. Jones</a>, <a title=\"Sam Jones (basketball, born 1933)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sam_Jones_(basketball,_born_1933)\">Sam Jones</a>, <a title=\"Satch Sanders\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satch_Sanders\">Satch Sanders</a>, and <a title=\"Bill Sharman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Sharman\">Bill Sharman</a>, would usher the Celtics into the greatest period in franchise history, winning eight consecutive NBA championships from 1959 to 1966. After Russell retired in 1969, the team entered a period of rebuilding. In the mid-1970s, the Celtics became contenders once again, winning two championships in <a title=\"1974 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1974_NBA_Finals\">1974</a> and <a title=\"1976 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1976_NBA_Finals\">1976</a> under the leadership of center <a title=\"Dave Cowens\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Cowens\">Dave Cowens</a>, forward <a title=\"John Havlicek\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Havlicek\">John Havlicek</a>, and point guard <a title=\"Jo Jo White\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jo_Jo_White\">Jo Jo White</a>.</p>\r\n<p>In the 1980s, the Celtics returned to dominance, as well as renewed competition with the <a title=\"Showtime (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Showtime_(basketball)\">\"Showtime\" Lakers</a>, who were led by <a title=\"Magic Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_Johnson\">Magic Johnson</a> and <a title=\"Kareem Abdul-Jabbar\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar\">Kareem Abdul-Jabbar</a>. Anchored by the \"Big Three\" of Larry Bird, <a title=\"Kevin McHale (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_McHale_(basketball)\">Kevin McHale</a>, and <a title=\"Robert Parish\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Parish\">Robert Parish</a>, the Celtics won championships in <a title=\"1981 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981_NBA_Finals\">1981</a>, <a title=\"1984 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984_NBA_Finals\">1984</a>, and <a title=\"1986 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986_NBA_Finals\">1986</a>. The team defeated the Lakers in the 1984 Finals, but lost to Los Angeles in <a title=\"1985 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985_NBA_Finals\">1985</a> and <a title=\"1987 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1987_NBA_Finals\">1987</a>. After the departure of Parish as a free agent, the retirement of both Bird and McHale, as well as the untimely death of star player <a title=\"Reggie Lewis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reggie_Lewis\">Reggie Lewis</a>, the team struggled through the 1990s and much of the early 2000s. It was not until the Celtics assembled a new \"Big Three\" of <a title=\"Kevin Garnett\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Garnett\">Kevin Garnett</a>, <a title=\"Paul Pierce\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Pierce\">Paul Pierce</a>, and <a title=\"Ray Allen\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Allen\">Ray Allen</a> that they found success once again. Under the leadership of head coach <a title=\"Doc Rivers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doc_Rivers\">Doc Rivers</a>, the team beat the Lakers to win a championship in <a title=\"2008 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_NBA_Finals\">2008</a>, but lost to Los Angeles in a seven-game series in <a title=\"2010 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_NBA_Finals\">2010</a>, the latest Finals matchup between the two ancient rivals.</p>\r\n<p>By the start of the 2013&ndash;14 season, none of the new \"Big Three\" were still with the team. <a title=\"Kevin Garnett\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Garnett\">Kevin Garnett</a> and <a title=\"Paul Pierce\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Pierce\">Paul Pierce</a> were traded away to the <a title=\"Brooklyn Nets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets\">Brooklyn Nets</a>, while Allen left as a free agent. After a period of rebuilding, the Celtics became a force again under head coach <a title=\"Brad Stevens\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brad_Stevens\">Brad Stevens</a>. During the <a title=\"2016&ndash;17 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_NBA_season\">2016&ndash;17 season</a>, the Celtics clinched the top seed in the Eastern Conference, but were eliminated in the Conference Finals. Led by <a title=\"Jaylen Brown\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaylen_Brown\">Jaylen Brown</a> and <a title=\"Jayson Tatum\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jayson_Tatum\">Jayson Tatum</a>, the team reached the Conference Finals four times over the following six years and returned to the NBA Finals in 2022, losing to the <a title=\"Golden State Warriors\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors\">Golden State Warriors</a>.</p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Franchise_history\" class=\"mw-headline\">Franchise history</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"History of the Boston Celtics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Boston_Celtics\">History of the Boston Celtics</a></div>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1946.E2.80.931950:_early_years\"></span><span id=\"1946&ndash;1950:_early_years\" class=\"mw-headline\">1946&ndash;1950: early years</span></h3>\r\n<p>The Boston Celtics were formed on June 6, 1946, by <a title=\"Boston Garden-Arena Corporation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Garden-Arena_Corporation\">Boston Garden-Arena Corporation</a> president <a title=\"Walter A. Brown\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_A._Brown\">Walter A. Brown</a> as a team in the <a title=\"Basketball Association of America\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball_Association_of_America\">Basketball Association of America</a>. In 1948, the team earned its first playoff appearance, only to lose to the <a title=\"Chicago Stags\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago_Stags\">Chicago Stags</a> 4&ndash;1. In 1949, the team missed the playoffs, fifth in the Eastern Division. Then, on August 3, 1949, the team became part of the <a title=\"National Basketball Association\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association\">National Basketball Association</a> after the absorption of the <a title=\"National Basketball League (United States)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_League_(United_States)\">National Basketball League</a> by the BAA.<sup id=\"cite_ref-13\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-13\">[13]</a></sup> In 1950, the Celtics signed <a title=\"Chuck Cooper (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuck_Cooper_(basketball)\">Chuck Cooper</a>, becoming the first NBA franchise to <a title=\"Draft (sports)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Draft_(sports)\">draft</a> a black player.<sup id=\"cite_ref-14\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-14\">[14]</a></sup> <a title=\"Chuck Connors\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuck_Connors\">Chuck Connors</a> of <em><a title=\"The Rifleman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Rifleman\">The Rifleman</a></em> fame was an original member of the Celtics in 1946.<sup id=\"cite_ref-15\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-15\">[15]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1950.E2.80.931957:_arrival_of_Bob_Cousy_and_Red_Auerbach\"></span><span id=\"1950&ndash;1957:_arrival_of_Bob_Cousy_and_Red_Auerbach\" class=\"mw-headline\">1950&ndash;1957: arrival of Bob Cousy and Red Auerbach</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 202px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bob_Cousy_NYWTS.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bob_Cousy_NYWTS.jpg/200px-Bob_Cousy_NYWTS.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bob_Cousy_NYWTS.jpg/300px-Bob_Cousy_NYWTS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bob_Cousy_NYWTS.jpg/400px-Bob_Cousy_NYWTS.jpg 2x\" width=\"200\" height=\"198\" data-file-width=\"2311\" data-file-height=\"2285\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 202px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Bob Cousy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Cousy\">Bob Cousy</a> played 13 years for the team, 6 of them ending in NBA titles</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The Celtics struggled during their early years, until the hiring of coach <a title=\"Red Auerbach\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Auerbach\">Red Auerbach</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-16\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-16\">[16]</a></sup> In the franchise's early days, Auerbach had no assistants, ran all the practices, did all the scouting&mdash;both of opposing teams and college draft prospects&mdash;and scheduled all road trips. One of the first great players to join the Celtics was <a title=\"Bob Cousy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Cousy\">Bob Cousy</a>, whom Auerbach initially refused to draft out of nearby <a title=\"College of the Holy Cross\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/College_of_the_Holy_Cross\">Holy Cross</a> because he was \"too flashy\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-17\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-17\">[17]</a></sup> Cousy's contract eventually became the property of the <a title=\"Chicago Stags\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago_Stags\">Chicago Stags</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-18\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-18\">[18]</a></sup> but when that franchise went bankrupt, Cousy went to the Celtics in a dispersal draft.</p>\r\n<p>After the <a title=\"1955&ndash;56 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1955%E2%80%9356_NBA_season\">1955&ndash;56 season</a>, Auerbach made a stunning trade, sending perennial All-Star <a title=\"Ed Macauley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ed_Macauley\">Ed Macauley</a> to the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"St. Louis Hawks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis_Hawks\">St. Louis Hawks</a> along with the draft rights to <a title=\"Cliff Hagan\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cliff_Hagan\">Cliff Hagan</a> for the second overall pick in the draft.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Hall_of_Fame_19-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-Hall_of_Fame-19\">[19]</a></sup> After negotiating with the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Rochester Royals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rochester_Royals\">Rochester Royals</a>&mdash;a negotiation that included a promise that the Celtics owner would send the highly sought-after <a title=\"Ice Capades\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_Capades\">Ice Capades</a> to Rochester if the Royals would let Russell slide to No. 2&mdash;Auerbach used the pick to select <a title=\"University of San Francisco\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_San_Francisco\">University of San Francisco</a> <a title=\"Center (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_(basketball)\">center</a> <a title=\"Bill Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Russell\">Bill Russell</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-20\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-20\">[20]</a></sup> Auerbach also acquired Holy Cross standout, and 1957 NBA Rookie of the Year, <a title=\"Tom Heinsohn\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Heinsohn\">Tom Heinsohn</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-recap1950s_21-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-recap1950s-21\">[21]</a></sup> Russell and Heinsohn worked extraordinarily well with Cousy, and they were the players around whom Auerbach would build the champion Celtics for more than a decade.<sup id=\"cite_ref-recap1950s_21-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-recap1950s-21\">[21]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1956.E2.80.931969:_Bill_Russell_era\"></span><span id=\"1956&ndash;1969:_Bill_Russell_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">1956&ndash;1969: Bill Russell era</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tmulti tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner multiimageinner\" style=\"width: 342px; max-width: 342px;\">\r\n<div class=\"trow\">\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 181px; max-width: 181px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 203px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bill_russell_dribbling_(cropped).jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bill_russell_dribbling_%28cropped%29.jpg/179px-Bill_russell_dribbling_%28cropped%29.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bill_russell_dribbling_%28cropped%29.jpg/269px-Bill_russell_dribbling_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bill_russell_dribbling_%28cropped%29.jpg/358px-Bill_russell_dribbling_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"179\" height=\"203\" data-file-width=\"691\" data-file-height=\"783\"></a></div>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Bill Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Russell\">Bill Russell</a> starred on 11 NBA title teams in 13 years as a Celtic</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 157px; max-width: 157px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 203px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sam_Jones,_Boston_Celtics,_1969.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sam_Jones%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_1969.jpg/155px-Sam_Jones%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_1969.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sam_Jones%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_1969.jpg/233px-Sam_Jones%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_1969.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sam_Jones%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_1969.jpg/310px-Sam_Jones%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_1969.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"155\" height=\"203\" data-file-width=\"318\" data-file-height=\"417\"></a></div>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Sam Jones (basketball, born 1933)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sam_Jones_(basketball,_born_1933)\">Sam Jones</a> played with the Celtics (1957&ndash;1969) winning 10 titles</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>With <a title=\"Bill Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Russell\">Bill Russell</a>, the Celtics advanced to the <a title=\"1957 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1957_NBA_Finals\">1957 NBA Finals</a> and defeated the St. Louis Hawks in seven games, the first of a record 17 championships. Russell went on to win 11 championships, making him the most decorated player in NBA history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-22\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-22\">[22]</a></sup> In 1958, the Celtics again advanced to the <a title=\"1958 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1958_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>, this time losing to the Hawks in 6 games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-23\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-23\">[23]</a></sup> However, with the acquisition of <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"K.C. Jones\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K.C._Jones\">K.C. Jones</a> that year, the Celtics began a dynasty that would last for more than a decade.<sup id=\"cite_ref-24\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-24\">[24]</a></sup> In 1959, the Celtics won the NBA championship after sweeping the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Minneapolis Lakers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minneapolis_Lakers\">Minneapolis Lakers</a>, the first of their record eight consecutive championships.<sup id=\"cite_ref-25\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-25\">[25]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>During that time, the Celtics met the Lakers in the Finals five times, starting an intense and often bitter rivalry that has spanned generations. In 1964, the Celtics became the first NBA team to have an all African-American starting lineup. On December 26, 1964, <a title=\"Willie Naulls\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willie_Naulls\">Willie Naulls</a> replaced an injured Tom Heinsohn, joining <a title=\"Satch Sanders\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satch_Sanders\">Tom 'Satch' Sanders</a>, K.C. Jones, <a title=\"Sam Jones (basketball, born 1933)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sam_Jones_(basketball,_born_1933)\">Sam Jones</a>, and Bill Russell in the starting lineup. The Celtics defeated St. Louis 97&ndash;84. Boston won its next 11 games with Naulls starting in place of Heinsohn.<sup id=\"cite_ref-26\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-26\">[26]</a></sup> The Celtics of the late 1950s&ndash;1960s are widely considered one of the most dominant teams of all time.<sup id=\"cite_ref-27\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-27\">[27]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Auerbach retired as coach after the 1965&ndash;66 season and Russell took over as player-coach, which was Auerbach's ploy to keep Russell interested.<sup id=\"cite_ref-28\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-28\">[28]</a></sup> With his appointment Russell became the first African-American coach in any U.S. pro sport. Auerbach would remain the general manager, a position he would hold well into the 1980s. However, the Celtics' string of NBA titles ended when they lost to the <a title=\"Philadelphia 76ers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philadelphia_76ers\">Philadelphia 76ers</a> in the 1967 Eastern Conference Finals. The aging team managed two more championships in 1968 and 1969, defeating the Los Angeles Lakers each time.<sup id=\"cite_ref-29\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-29\">[29]</a></sup> Russell retired after the 1969 season, effectively ending a Celtics dynasty that had garnered an unrivaled 11 NBA titles in 13 seasons.<sup id=\"cite_ref-30\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-30\">[30]</a></sup> The team's run of 8 consecutive is the longest championship streak in U.S. professional sports history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-31\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-31\">[31]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1970.E2.80.931978:_Cowens.E2.80.93Havlicek.E2.80.93White_era\"></span><span id=\"1970&ndash;1978:_Cowens&ndash;Havlicek&ndash;White_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">1970&ndash;1978: Cowens&ndash;Havlicek&ndash;White era</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tmulti tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner multiimageinner\" style=\"width: 342px; max-width: 342px;\">\r\n<div class=\"trow\">\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 161px; max-width: 161px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 237px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:John_Havlicek_1960s.jpeg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/John_Havlicek_1960s.jpeg/159px-John_Havlicek_1960s.jpeg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/John_Havlicek_1960s.jpeg/239px-John_Havlicek_1960s.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/John_Havlicek_1960s.jpeg/318px-John_Havlicek_1960s.jpeg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"159\" height=\"238\" data-file-width=\"1244\" data-file-height=\"1860\"></a></div>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"John Havlicek\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Havlicek\">John Havlicek</a>, 16 years with the Celtics</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 177px; max-width: 177px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 237px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dave_Cowens.jpeg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Dave_Cowens.jpeg/175px-Dave_Cowens.jpeg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Dave_Cowens.jpeg/263px-Dave_Cowens.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Dave_Cowens.jpeg/350px-Dave_Cowens.jpeg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"175\" height=\"238\" data-file-width=\"1584\" data-file-height=\"2150\"></a></div>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Dave Cowens\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Cowens\">Dave Cowens</a>, two titles and MVP in 1973</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The 1969&ndash;70 season was a rebuilding year, as the Celtics had their first losing record since the <a title=\"1949&ndash;50 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949%E2%80%9350_NBA_season\">1949&ndash;50 season</a>. However, with the acquisition of <a title=\"Paul Silas\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Silas\">Paul Silas</a> and future Hall of Famers <a title=\"Dave Cowens\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Cowens\">Dave Cowens</a><sup id=\"cite_ref-32\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-32\">[32]</a></sup> and <a title=\"Jo Jo White\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jo_Jo_White\">Jo Jo White</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-33\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-33\">[33]</a></sup> the Celtics soon became dominant again. After losing in the Eastern Conference Finals in 1972, the Celtics regrouped and came out determined in 1973 and posted an excellent 68&ndash;14 regular-season record. But the season ended in disappointment, as they were upset in seven games by the <a title=\"New York Knicks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Knicks\">New York Knicks</a> in the Conference Finals. <a title=\"John Havlicek\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Havlicek\">John Havlicek</a> injured his right shoulder in game six and was forced to play game seven shooting left-handed.<sup id=\"cite_ref-34\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-34\">[34]</a></sup> The Celtics returned to the playoffs the next year, defeating the <a title=\"Milwaukee Bucks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milwaukee_Bucks\">Milwaukee Bucks</a> in the <a title=\"1974 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1974_NBA_Finals\">1974 NBA Finals</a> for their 12th NBA championship.<sup id=\"cite_ref-35\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-35\">[35]</a></sup> Boston took a 3&ndash;2 series lead and had a chance to claim the title on their home court. The Bucks won Game Six in Boston when <a title=\"Kareem Abdul-Jabbar\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar\">Kareem Abdul-Jabbar</a> nestled in a hook shot with 3&nbsp;seconds left in the game's second overtime, and the series returned to Milwaukee. Cowens was the hero in Game 7, scoring 28 points, as the Celtics brought the title back to Boston for the first time in five years.</p>\r\n<p>In 1976, the team won yet another championship, defeating the <a title=\"Phoenix Suns\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phoenix_Suns\">Phoenix Suns</a> in six games. The Finals featured one of the greatest games in NBA history. With the series tied at two games apiece, the Suns trailed early in the Boston Garden, but came back to force overtime. In double overtime, a <a title=\"Gar Heard\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gar_Heard\">Gar Heard</a> turn-around jumper at the top of the key sent the game to a third overtime, at which point the Celtics prevailed.<sup id=\"cite_ref-36\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-36\">[36]</a></sup> After the 1976 championship and a <a title=\"1977 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_NBA_playoffs\">playoff appearance in 1977</a>, Boston went into another rebuilding phase. In the <a title=\"1977 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_NBA_draft\">1977 NBA draft</a>, the Celtics drafted a young forward from <a title=\"University of North Carolina at Charlotte\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Charlotte\">UNC Charlotte</a> named <a title=\"Cedric Maxwell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cedric_Maxwell\">Cedric Maxwell</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-37\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-37\">[37]</a></sup> \"Cornbread\" Maxwell did not contribute much in his rookie season, but he showed promise. Auerbach's job became even tougher following the <a title=\"1977&ndash;78 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977%E2%80%9378_NBA_season\">1977&ndash;78 season</a> in which they went 32&ndash;50 as Havlicek, the Celtics' all-time leading scorer, retired after 16 seasons.<sup id=\"cite_ref-38\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-38\">[38]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Celtics owned two of the top eight picks in the <a title=\"1978 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978_NBA_draft\">1978 NBA draft</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-39\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-39\">[39]</a></sup> Auerbach took a risk by selecting junior <a title=\"Larry Bird\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_Bird\">Larry Bird</a> of <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Indiana State\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indiana_State\">Indiana State</a> with the sixth overall pick, knowing that Bird would stay in college for his senior year but believing that his potential would make him worth the wait. The team retained Bird's rights for one year and signed him soon after he led Indiana State to the NCAA championship game. In 1978, Celtics owner <a title=\"Irv Levin\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irv_Levin\">Irv Levin</a> traded franchises with <a title=\"Buffalo Braves\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buffalo_Braves\">Buffalo Braves</a> owner <a title=\"John Y. Brown Jr.\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Y._Brown_Jr.\">John Y. Brown Jr.</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-40\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-40\">[40]</a></sup> Two weeks before the swap of franchises was made official, details of a six-player trade between the two teams were reported. Boston sent <a title=\"Freeman Williams\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freeman_Williams\">Freeman Williams</a>, <a title=\"Kevin Kunnert\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Kunnert\">Kevin Kunnert</a>, and <a title=\"Kermit Washington\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kermit_Washington\">Kermit Washington</a> to the Braves for \"Tiny\" Archibald, Billy Knight, and <a title=\"Marvin Barnes\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvin_Barnes\">Marvin Barnes</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-auto_41-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-auto-41\">[41]</a></sup> The move turned Boston fans against Brown, both because Kunnert and Washington were seen as key pieces of the team's future and because Auerbach publicly stated that he was not consulted about the trade.<sup id=\"cite_ref-auto_41-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-auto-41\">[41]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1979.E2.80.931992:_Larry_Bird_era\"></span><span id=\"1979&ndash;1992:_Larry_Bird_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">1979&ndash;1992: Larry Bird era</span></h3>\r\n<p>The relationship between Brown and Auerbach worsened with Brown's decision to acquire <a title=\"Bob McAdoo\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_McAdoo\">Bob McAdoo</a> in February 1979,<sup id=\"cite_ref-42\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-42\">[42]</a></sup> in exchange for three first-round draft picks that Auerbach had planned to use to rebuild the franchise.<sup id=\"cite_ref-auto1_43-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-auto1-43\">[43]</a></sup> Again, Brown made the trade without consulting Auerbach.<sup id=\"cite_ref-44\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-44\">[44]</a></sup> Auerbach almost left Boston to take a job with the New York Knicks as a result.<sup id=\"cite_ref-auto1_43-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-auto1-43\">[43]</a></sup> With public support strongly behind Auerbach, Brown sold the team to <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Harry Mangurian\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Mangurian\">Harry Mangurian</a> in 1979 rather than run the risk of losing his famed general manager.<sup id=\"cite_ref-45\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-45\">[45]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-autogenerated1_46-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-autogenerated1-46\">[46]</a></sup> The Celtics would struggle through the season, going 29&ndash;53.<sup id=\"cite_ref-47\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-47\">[47]</a></sup> Newcomers <a title=\"Chris Ford\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Ford\">Chris Ford</a>, <a title=\"Rick Robey\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rick_Robey\">Rick Robey</a>, <a title=\"Cedric Maxwell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cedric_Maxwell\">Cedric Maxwell</a> and <a title=\"Nate Archibald\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nate_Archibald\">Nate Archibald</a> failed to reverse the team's momentum.<sup id=\"cite_ref-48\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-48\">[48]</a></sup></p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 201px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Larry_Bird_Lipofsky.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2f/Larry_Bird_Lipofsky.jpg\" width=\"199\" height=\"250\" data-file-width=\"199\" data-file-height=\"250\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 201px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">12 time All-Star <a title=\"Larry Bird\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_Bird\">Larry Bird</a> played in the Celtics from 1979 to 1992. He is widely regarded as one of the greatest basketball players of all time.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>Larry Bird debuted for the Celtics during the <a title=\"1979&ndash;80 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979%E2%80%9380_NBA_season\">1979&ndash;80 season</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-49\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-49\">[49]</a></sup> With a new owner in place, Auerbach made a number of moves that would bring the team back to prominence. He almost immediately traded McAdoo,<sup id=\"cite_ref-50\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-50\">[50]</a></sup> a former NBA scoring champion, to the <a title=\"Detroit Pistons\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Detroit_Pistons\">Detroit Pistons</a> for <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Guard (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guard_(basketball)\">guard</a> <a title=\"M. L. Carr\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M._L._Carr\">M. L. Carr</a>, a defensive specialist, and two first-round picks in the <a title=\"1980 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980_NBA_draft\">1980 NBA draft</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-autogenerated1_46-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-autogenerated1-46\">[46]</a></sup> He also picked up <a title=\"Point guard\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Point_guard\">point guard</a> <a title=\"Gerald Henderson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_Henderson\">Gerald Henderson</a> from the <a title=\"Continental Basketball Association\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_Basketball_Association\">CBA</a>. Carr, Archibald, Henderson and Ford formed a highly competent backcourt, blending in well with the talented frontcourt of Cowens, Maxwell and Bird. With Bird winning <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"NBA Rookie of the Year\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Rookie_of_the_Year\">NBA Rookie of the Year</a> honors<sup id=\"cite_ref-51\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-51\">[51]</a></sup> the team went 61&ndash;21, a 32-game improvement from the previous season. Playing strong in the playoffs, the Celtics fell to the Philadelphia 76ers in the Eastern Conference Finals.<sup id=\"cite_ref-52\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-52\">[52]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>After the season, Auerbach completed one of the most lopsided trades in NBA history, garnering a pair of future Hall of Famers for a pair of first-round draft picks. Seeking to improve the team immediately, Auerbach sent the team's two first-round draft picks to the <a title=\"Golden State Warriors\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors\">Golden State Warriors</a> for both <a title=\"Center (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_(basketball)\">center</a> <a title=\"Robert Parish\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Parish\">Robert Parish</a><sup id=\"cite_ref-parish_53-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-parish-53\">[53]</a></sup> and the Warriors' first round pick. He then used the pick the Celtics obtained from Golden State to select <a title=\"University of Minnesota\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Minnesota\">University of Minnesota</a> <a title=\"Power forward (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_forward_(basketball)\">power forward</a> <a title=\"Kevin McHale (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_McHale_(basketball)\">Kevin McHale</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-54\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-54\">[54]</a></sup> The \"Big Three\" of Bird, McHale and Parish played together for the Celtics until 1992, won three NBA championships together,<sup id=\"cite_ref-55\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-55\">[55]</a></sup> and were later described as the best NBA frontcourt of all time.<sup id=\"cite_ref-56\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-56\">[56]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-57\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-57\">[57]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-birdbio_58-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-birdbio-58\">[58]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-59\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-59\">[59]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Despite losing <a title=\"Center (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_(basketball)\">center</a> <a title=\"Dave Cowens\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Cowens\">Dave Cowens</a> to retirement late in training camp, the Celtics went 62&ndash;20 under coach <a title=\"Bill Fitch\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Fitch\">Bill Fitch</a> in <a title=\"1980&ndash;81 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_NBA_season\">1980&ndash;81</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-60\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-60\">[60]</a></sup> Once again, the Celtics faced the 76ers in the Eastern Conference Finals, falling behind 3&ndash;1 before coming back to win Game Seven, 91&ndash;90. The Celtics went on to win the 1981 NBA championship over the <a title=\"Houston Rockets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houston_Rockets\">Houston Rockets</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-61\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-61\">[61]</a></sup> with Maxwell being named <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"NBA Finals MVP\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Finals_MVP\">NBA Finals MVP</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-62\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-62\">[62]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Following the <a title=\"1981&ndash;82 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_NBA_season\">1981&ndash;82 season</a>, the Celtics once again met the 76ers in the playoffs. This time, they lost in seven games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-63\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-63\">[63]</a></sup> In <a title=\"1982&ndash;83 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_NBA_season\">1983</a> the Celtics were swept in the playoffs (a first for the franchise) by the Milwaukee Bucks;<sup id=\"cite_ref-64\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-64\">[64]</a></sup> afterwards, Fitch resigned and the team was sold to new owners led by <a title=\"Don Gaston\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don_Gaston\">Don Gaston</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-gaston_65-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-gaston-65\">[65]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In <a title=\"1983&ndash;84 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1983%E2%80%9384_NBA_season\">1983&ndash;84</a>, the Celtics under new coach <a title=\"K. C. Jones\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K._C._Jones\">K. C. Jones</a> would go 62&ndash;20 and return to the <a title=\"1984 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a> after a three-year hiatus.<sup id=\"cite_ref-66\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-66\">[66]</a></sup> Boston came back from a 2&ndash;1 deficit to defeat the Lakers for their 15th championship.<sup id=\"cite_ref-67\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-67\">[67]</a></sup> Bird renewed his college rivalry with Lakers star <a title=\"Magic Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_Johnson\">Magic Johnson</a> during this series. After the season, Auerbach officially retired as general manager, but maintained the position of team president.<sup id=\"cite_ref-red_68-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-red-68\">[68]</a></sup> He was succeeded by <a title=\"Jan Volk\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Volk\">Jan Volk</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-red_68-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-red-68\">[68]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 1985, the Lakers and Celtics met again in the Finals, with the Lakers winning.<sup id=\"cite_ref-69\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-69\">[69]</a></sup> This was the first time the Lakers had defeated the Celtics in the Finals and the only time the team had won a championship at Boston Garden. During the following off-season, the Celtics acquired <a title=\"Bill Walton\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Walton\">Bill Walton</a> from the <a title=\"Los Angeles Clippers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Clippers\">Los Angeles Clippers</a> in exchange for <a title=\"Cedric Maxwell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cedric_Maxwell\">Cedric Maxwell</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-70\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-70\">[70]</a></sup> Walton had been an All-Star and league MVP while leading the <a title=\"Portland Trail Blazers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portland_Trail_Blazers\">Portland Trail Blazers</a> to the 1977 NBA championship, but injuries had hobbled him since. Considered the best passing center in NBA history, he stayed healthy and was a big part of the Celtics' success in 1986.</p>\r\n<p>The Celtics won the second pick in the <a title=\"1986 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986_NBA_draft\">1986 NBA draft</a> and drafted <a title=\"University of Maryland, College Park\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Maryland,_College_Park\">University of Maryland</a> star <a title=\"Len Bias\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Len_Bias\">Len Bias</a>, one of the most heralded prospects of his era.<sup id=\"cite_ref-71\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-71\">[71]</a></sup> Bias died 36 hours later of an accidental cocaine overdose.<sup id=\"cite_ref-72\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-72\">[72]</a></sup> Despite the tragedy, the Celtics remained competitive in <a title=\"1986&ndash;87 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_NBA_season\">1986&ndash;87</a>, going 59&ndash;23 and again winning the Eastern Conference Championship.<sup id=\"cite_ref-73\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-73\">[73]</a></sup> They were defeated in the Finals by the Lakers in six games.</p>\r\n<p>In 1988, the Celtics lost in six games to the Detroit Pistons in the Eastern Conference Finals.<sup id=\"cite_ref-74\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-74\">[74]</a></sup> Following the season, head coach <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"K.C. Jones\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K.C._Jones\">K.C. Jones</a> retired and was replaced by assistant <a title=\"Jimmy Rodgers (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Rodgers_(basketball)\">Jimmy Rodgers</a>. Boston's hopes for <a title=\"1988&ndash;89 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_NBA_season\">1988&ndash;89</a> faded when Bird underwent a procedure to remove bone spurs in his feet early in the season, and the Celtics won just 42 games before a first-round playoff defeat to the Pistons. Bird returned in <a title=\"1989&ndash;90 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_NBA_season\">1989&ndash;90</a> and led the Celtics to a 52&ndash;30 record. In the <a title=\"1990 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a>, the Celtics collapsed after winning the first two games in a best-of-five series against the New York Knicks, losing three straight games and the series. After the playoffs, Rodgers was fired and replaced by assistant coach and former Celtics player <a title=\"Chris Ford\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Ford\">Chris Ford</a>.</p>\r\n<p>Under Ford's leadership, the Celtics improved to 56&ndash;26 in <a title=\"1990&ndash;91 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_NBA_season\">1990&ndash;91</a>, recapturing the Atlantic Division title even though Bird missed 22 games with several injuries. The Celtics again lost to the Pistons in the playoffs. In 1992, a late-season rally allowed a 51&ndash;31 Celtics team to catch the New York Knicks and repeat as Atlantic Division champions. After sweeping the Indiana Pacers in the first round, the Celtics lost a seven-game Eastern Conference Semifinals series to the <a title=\"Cleveland Cavaliers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cleveland_Cavaliers\">Cleveland Cavaliers</a>. Back injuries limited Bird to only 45 regular-season games, and just four of ten in the playoffs. After thirteen NBA seasons and a gold medal at the <a title=\"1992 Summer Olympics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics\">Barcelona Olympics</a> with the <a title=\"United States men's national basketball team\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_basketball_team\">Dream Team</a>, continued back trouble led Bird to retire in 1992.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1993.E2.80.931998:_tragedy_and_decline\"></span><span id=\"1993&ndash;1998:_tragedy_and_decline\" class=\"mw-headline\">1993&ndash;1998: tragedy and decline</span></h3>\r\n<p>The loss of Bird and the aging of the team's other veteran stars forced coach Chris Ford into rebuilding mode.<sup id=\"cite_ref-75\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-75\">[75]</a></sup> Hopes centered on 26-year-old <a title=\"Reggie Lewis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reggie_Lewis\">Reggie Lewis</a>, a <a title=\"Small forward\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_forward\">small forward</a> out of Boston's <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Northeastern University (Boston)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northeastern_University_(Boston)\">Northeastern University</a>. In the <a title=\"1993 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993_NBA_playoffs\">first round of the 1993 playoffs</a> Lewis fainted during Boston's four-game series loss by the <a title=\"Charlotte Hornets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets\">Charlotte Hornets</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-76\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-76\">[76]</a></sup> An examination revealed heart problems,<sup id=\"cite_ref-77\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-77\">[77]</a></sup> but Lewis was able to get doctors to clear him for a comeback. Before he could make it he died of a heart attack while shooting baskets at Brandeis University during the off-season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-78\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-78\">[78]</a></sup> The Celtics honored his memory by retiring his number 35.<sup id=\"cite_ref-lewis_79-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-lewis-79\">[79]</a></sup> With McHale having retired after the Celtics' playoff loss to the Hornets, Boston's original Big 3 era came to an end in 1994 upon Robert Parish's signing with Charlotte.<sup id=\"cite_ref-parish_53-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-parish-53\">[53]</a></sup> The team collapsed, finishing out of the playoffs with a 32&ndash;50 mark.</p>\r\n<p>In 1994, the Celtics hired former player and legendary towel-waving cheerleader <a title=\"M. L. Carr\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M._L._Carr\">M. L. Carr</a> as the team's new vice president of basketball operations. Working alongside general manager <a title=\"Jan Volk\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Volk\">Jan Volk</a>, Carr selected <a title=\"University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill\">University of North Carolina</a> star <a title=\"Eric Montross\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Montross\">Eric Montross</a> with Boston's first-round pick in the <a title=\"1994 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1994_NBA_draft\">1994 NBA draft</a>. Montross became the new heir apparent in the paint, but failed to develop and was eventually traded. <a title=\"1994&ndash;95 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_NBA_season\">1994&ndash;95</a> was the Celtics' final season in the <a title=\"Boston Garden\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Garden\">Boston Garden</a>. The Celtics signed aging <a title=\"Dominique Wilkins\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominique_Wilkins\">Dominique Wilkins</a> as a free agent, who led the team in scoring with 17.8 PPG. Second-year player <a title=\"Dino Rađa\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dino_Ra%C4%91a\">Dino Rađa</a>, a power forward from <a title=\"Croatia\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croatia\">Croatia</a>, added an interior presence the team had been lacking in <a title=\"1993&ndash;94 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_NBA_season\">1993&ndash;94</a>. The Celtics made the playoffs, losing to the heavily favored <a title=\"Orlando Magic\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orlando_Magic\">Orlando Magic</a> in four games. In 1995, the Celtics moved from the Boston Garden to the Fleet Center (later TD BankNorth, then <a title=\"TD Garden\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TD_Garden\">TD Garden</a>). Carr fired <a title=\"Chris Ford\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Ford\">Chris Ford</a> and took the coaching reins himself. After drafting <a title=\"Providence College\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Providence_College\">Providence College</a> star Eric Williams, the Celtics struggled to a 33&ndash;49 record.</p>\r\n<p>Things got worse in <a title=\"1996&ndash;97 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_NBA_season\">1996&ndash;97</a> as the Celtics lost a franchise-record 67 games, setting an unwanted <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Imperfect season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperfect_season\">NBA record</a> winning only once against other Atlantic Division teams and just fifteen victories overall. In spite of the emergence of 1st-round draft pick <a title=\"Antoine Walker\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antoine_Walker\">Antoine Walker</a>, Carr resigned after the season ended, while <a title=\"Rick Pitino\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rick_Pitino\">Rick Pitino</a> was hired to join the franchise as the team's president, director of basketball operations, and <a title=\"Head coach\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_coach\">head coach</a>, reportedly on a $70 million ten-year contract. Volk resigned on May 7, 1997.<sup id=\"cite_ref-80\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-80\">[80]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-81\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-81\">[81]</a></sup> Pitino's appointment as team president was controversial as Auerbach, the incumbent who had filled that role for more than 25 years, first heard about the change from local media. Unfortunately for the franchise, Pitino was not the savior everyone hoped he would be. Auerbach bore the insult of being elbowed out with dignity, even as the team failed to improve.</p>\r\n<p>The Celtics received the third and sixth draft picks in the <a title=\"1997 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1997_NBA_draft\">1997 NBA draft</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-82\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-82\">[82]</a></sup> and used the picks to select a brand new backcourt through <a title=\"Chauncey Billups\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chauncey_Billups\">Chauncey Billups</a> and <a title=\"Ron Mercer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ron_Mercer\">Ron Mercer</a>. The young team that lost 67 games the year before was dismantled, with <a title=\"David Wesley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Wesley\">David Wesley</a>, <a title=\"Dino Rađa\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dino_Ra%C4%91a\">Dino Rađa</a> and <a title=\"Rick Fox\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rick_Fox\">Rick Fox</a> being let go, and Williams traded to the <a title=\"Denver Nuggets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denver_Nuggets\">Denver Nuggets</a> for a pair of second round draft picks (Williams would return to the Celtics in 1999 and played for four years). <a title=\"Walter McCarty\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_McCarty\">Walter McCarty</a> was also acquired in a trade with the Knicks. With a promising start, upsetting the defending champions <a title=\"Chicago Bulls\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago_Bulls\">Chicago Bulls</a> at home on opening night,<sup id=\"cite_ref-83\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-83\">[83]</a></sup> and hard play from the youngsters that led to leaderships in turnovers and steals, the team improved its victories from 15 to 36 despite many losing streaks.<sup id=\"cite_ref-84\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-84\">[84]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-85\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-85\">[85]</a></sup> Billups was subsequently traded to the Raptors during his rookie year,<sup id=\"cite_ref-86\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-86\">[86]</a></sup> and Mercer was traded to the Nuggets during his third season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-87\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-87\">[87]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1998.E2.80.932013:_Paul_Pierce_era\"></span><span id=\"1998&ndash;2013:_Paul_Pierce_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">1998&ndash;2013: Paul Pierce era</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Paul_Pierce_2008-01-13.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Paul_Pierce_2008-01-13.jpg/170px-Paul_Pierce_2008-01-13.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Paul_Pierce_2008-01-13.jpg/255px-Paul_Pierce_2008-01-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Paul_Pierce_2008-01-13.jpg/340px-Paul_Pierce_2008-01-13.jpg 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"255\" data-file-width=\"2074\" data-file-height=\"3110\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tleft\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">Drafted by the Celtics in 1998, <a title=\"Paul Pierce\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Pierce\">Paul Pierce</a> went on to star for the Celtics and later won the NBA Finals MVP Award when the team won the NBA championship in 2008</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The following year in the <a title=\"1998 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_NBA_draft\">1998 NBA draft</a>, the Celtics drafted <a title=\"Paul Pierce\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Pierce\">Paul Pierce</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-88\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-88\">[88]</a></sup> a college star who had been expected to be drafted much earlier than the Celtics' 10th overall pick. Pierce had an immediate impact during the lockout-shortened <a title=\"1998&ndash;99 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_NBA_season\">1998&ndash;99 season</a>, averaging 19.5 points and being named <a title=\"NBA Rookie of the Month Award\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Rookie_of_the_Month_Award\">Rookie of The Month</a> in February as he led the league in steals.<sup id=\"cite_ref-89\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-89\">[89]</a></sup> However, the Celtics continued to struggle as Pitino failed to achieve meaningful success. After Boston lost to the <a title=\"Toronto Raptors\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toronto_Raptors\">Toronto Raptors</a> on March 1, 2000, on a buzzer-beater by <a title=\"Vince Carter\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vince_Carter\">Vince Carter</a>, Pitino delivered the memorable \"walking through that door\" speech, invoking Bird, McHale and Parish, which has been frequently cited over the years as a reality check for organizations wrestling with bygone glory.<sup id=\"cite_ref-90\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-90\">[90]</a></sup> He resigned in January 2001.<sup id=\"cite_ref-91\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-91\">[91]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Following the resignation of Rick Pitino, the Celtics saw modest improvement under coach <a title=\"Jim O'Brien (basketball, born 1952)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_O%27Brien_(basketball,_born_1952)\">Jim O'Brien</a>. <a title=\"Paul Pierce\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Pierce\">Paul Pierce</a> matured into an NBA star and was ably complemented by Antoine Walker and the other players acquired over the years. While the team was 12&ndash;21 when Pitino left, O'Brien's record to finish the season was 24&ndash;24.<sup id=\"cite_ref-92\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-92\">[92]</a></sup> Following the <a title=\"2000&ndash;01 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_NBA_season\">2000&ndash;01 season</a> O'Brien was given the job of head coach on a permanent basis. As a result of numerous trades, the Celtics had three picks in the <a title=\"2001 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001_NBA_draft\">2001 NBA draft</a>. They selected <a title=\"Joe Johnson (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Johnson_(basketball)\">Joe Johnson</a>, <a title=\"Joseph Forte\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Forte\">Joe Forte</a>, and <a title=\"Kedrick Brown\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kedrick_Brown\">Kedrick Brown</a>. Only Johnson managed to succeed in the NBA, becoming a perennial All-Star after leaving the Celtics.</p>\r\n<p>The Celtics entered the <a title=\"2001&ndash;02 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_NBA_season\">2001&ndash;02 season</a> with low expectations. The team's success in the latter stages of 2000&ndash;01 was largely forgotten, and critics were surprised when the team, along with the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"New Jersey Nets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Jersey_Nets\">New Jersey Nets</a>, surged to the top of the <a title=\"Atlantic Division (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Division_(NBA)\">Atlantic Division</a> ahead of the Philadelphia 76ers, who were fresh off a trip to the <a title=\"2001 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>. The Celtics won a hard-fought 5-game series with the 76ers in the first round, 3&ndash;2. Pierce scored 46 points in the series-clinching blowout at the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"FleetCenter (Boston)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FleetCenter_(Boston)\">Fleet Center</a>. In the Conference Semifinals, the Celtics defeated the favored Detroit Pistons 4&ndash;1. In their first trip to the <a title=\"Eastern Conference (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Conference_(NBA)\">Eastern Conference</a> Finals since <a title=\"1988 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_NBA_playoffs\">1988</a>, the Celtics jumped out to a 2&ndash;1 series lead over the Nets, after rallying from 21 points down in the fourth quarter to win Game 3, but would lose the next three games to fall 4&ndash;2.<sup id=\"cite_ref-93\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-93\">[93]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2003, the Celtics were sold by owner Paul Gaston to Boston Basketball Partners L.L.C.,<sup id=\"cite_ref-nba.com_94-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-nba.com-94\">[94]</a></sup> led by <a title=\"H. Irving Grousbeck\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H._Irving_Grousbeck\">H. Irving Grousbeck</a>, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Wycliffe Grousbeck\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wycliffe_Grousbeck\">Wycliffe Grousbeck</a> and <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Steve Pagliuca\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Pagliuca\">Steve Pagliuca</a>. The team made it back to the <a title=\"2003 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a> but were swept by the Nets in the second round, despite bringing Game 4 to double overtime.<sup id=\"cite_ref-95\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-95\">[95]</a></sup> Before their elimination, the team hired former Celtics' guard <a title=\"Danny Ainge\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danny_Ainge\">Danny Ainge</a> as general manager, moving Chris Wallace to another position in the organization. Ainge believed the team had reached its peak and promptly sent Antoine Walker to the <a title=\"Dallas Mavericks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks\">Dallas Mavericks</a> (along with <a title=\"Tony Delk\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Delk\">Tony Delk</a>).<sup id=\"cite_ref-96\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-96\">[96]</a></sup> In return, the Celtics received the often-injured <a title=\"Raef LaFrentz\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raef_LaFrentz\">Raef LaFrentz</a>, <a title=\"Chris Mills (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Mills_(basketball)\">Chris Mills</a>, <a title=\"Jiř&iacute; Welsch\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ji%C5%99%C3%AD_Welsch\">Jiř&iacute; Welsch</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-97\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-97\">[97]</a></sup> and a first-round pick in <a title=\"2004 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_NBA_draft\">2004</a>. The Celtics made the <a title=\"2004 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a>, only to be swept in the first round by the Indiana Pacers, losing all four games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-98\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-98\">[98]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h4><span id=\"2004.E2.80.932007:_arrival_of_Doc_Rivers\"></span><span id=\"2004&ndash;2007:_arrival_of_Doc_Rivers\" class=\"mw-headline\">2004&ndash;2007: arrival of Doc Rivers</span></h4>\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 152px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Doc_Rivers.JPG\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Doc_Rivers.JPG/150px-Doc_Rivers.JPG\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Doc_Rivers.JPG/225px-Doc_Rivers.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Doc_Rivers.JPG/300px-Doc_Rivers.JPG 2x\" width=\"150\" height=\"224\" data-file-width=\"2592\" data-file-height=\"3872\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 152px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">Head coach <a title=\"Doc Rivers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doc_Rivers\">Doc Rivers</a> led the Celtics to an NBA title in 2008.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The Celtics were a young team under new coach <a title=\"Doc Rivers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doc_Rivers\">Doc Rivers</a> during the 2004&ndash;05 season,<sup id=\"cite_ref-99\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-99\">[99]</a></sup> having drafted youngsters <a title=\"Al Jefferson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Jefferson\">Al Jefferson</a>, <a title=\"Delonte West\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delonte_West\">Delonte West</a> and <a title=\"Tony Allen (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Allen_(basketball)\">Tony Allen</a> in the 2004 Draft. Yet they seemed to have a core of good young players, led by Pierce and rookie <a title=\"Al Jefferson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Jefferson\">Al Jefferson</a>, to go along with a group of able veterans. The Celtics went 45&ndash;37 and won their first <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"NBA Atlantic Division\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Atlantic_Division\">Atlantic Division</a> title since <a title=\"1991&ndash;92 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_NBA_season\">1991&ndash;92</a>, receiving a boost from returning star Antoine Walker in mid-season. The Pacers defeated them in the first round yet again, with the series culminating in an embarrassing 27-point loss in Game 7 at the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"FleetCenter (Boston)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FleetCenter_(Boston)\">Fleet Center</a>. After the season Walker was traded again, this time to the <a title=\"Miami Heat\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miami_Heat\">Miami Heat</a>. Despite Pierce's career season, in which he averaged career-highs in points (26.8), the Celtics missed the playoffs with a 33&ndash;49 record, owing largely to a young roster and constant roster shuffling, which saw the likes of <a title=\"Marcus Banks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Banks\">Marcus Banks</a>, <a title=\"Ricky Davis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ricky_Davis\">Ricky Davis</a> and <a title=\"Mark Blount\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Blount\">Mark Blount</a> traded for underachieving former first-overall pick <a title=\"Michael Olowokandi\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Olowokandi\">Michael Olowokandi</a> and former all-star <a title=\"Wally Szczerbiak\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wally_Szczerbiak\">Wally Szczerbiak</a>.</p>\r\n<p>The Celtics continued to rebuild in the <a title=\"2006 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_NBA_draft\">2006 NBA draft</a>. The Celtics selected Kentucky point guard <a title=\"Rajon Rondo\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajon_Rondo\">Rajon Rondo</a>, who was to become a key piece in the team's revival. In the second round the Celtics added center <a title=\"Leon Powe\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Powe\">Leon Powe</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-100\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-100\">[100]</a></sup> The <a title=\"2006&ndash;07 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NBA_season\">2006&ndash;07 season</a> was a gloomy one for the franchise, starting with the death of Red Auerbach at 89. Auerbach was one of the few remaining people who had been a part of the NBA since its inception in 1946.<sup id=\"cite_ref-101\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-101\">[101]</a></sup> The Celtics went 2&ndash;22 from late December 2006 through early February 2007 after losing Pierce to injury, the result of a stress reaction in his left foot. At first, the Celtics received a much-needed boost from guard <a title=\"Tony Allen (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Allen_(basketball)\">Tony Allen</a> but he tore his <a title=\"Anterior cruciate ligament\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anterior_cruciate_ligament\">ACL</a> and <a title=\"Medial collateral ligament\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medial_collateral_ligament\">MCL</a> on a needless dunk attempt after the whistle.<sup id=\"cite_ref-102\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-102\">[102]</a></sup> The Celtics compiled a record of 24&ndash;58, second-worst in the NBA, including a franchise-record <a title=\"List of National Basketball Association longest losing streaks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_National_Basketball_Association_longest_losing_streaks\">18-game losing streak</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-103\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-103\">[103]</a></sup> At the end of the season, the Celtics, with the second-worst record in the NBA, were at least hopeful that they could secure a high draft pick and select either <a title=\"Greg Oden\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greg_Oden\">Greg Oden</a> or <a title=\"Kevin Durant\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Durant\">Kevin Durant</a> to help rebuild the franchise, but the Celtics fell to fifth in the Draft Lottery.</p>\r\n<h4><span id=\"2007.E2.80.932012:_new_.22Big_Three.22:_Pierce.2C_Allen.2C_and_Garnett_era\"></span><span id=\"2007&ndash;2012:_new_&quot;Big_Three&quot;:_Pierce,_Allen,_and_Garnett_era\" class=\"mw-headline\"><span id=\"The_new_big_three\" class=\"anchor\"></span> 2007&ndash;2012: new \"Big Three\": Pierce, Allen, and Garnett era</span></h4>\r\n<p>In the summer of 2007, general manager <a title=\"Danny Ainge\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danny_Ainge\">Danny Ainge</a> made a series of moves that returned the Celtics to prominence. On draft night, he traded No. 5 pick <a title=\"Jeff Green (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeff_Green_(basketball)\">Jeff Green</a>, <a title=\"Wally Szczerbiak\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wally_Szczerbiak\">Wally Szczerbiak</a> and <a title=\"Delonte West\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delonte_West\">Delonte West</a> to Seattle for perennial All-Star <a title=\"Ray Allen\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Allen\">Ray Allen</a> and Seattle's second-round pick, which the team used to select LSU's <a title=\"Glen Davis (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glen_Davis_(basketball)\">Glen \"Big Baby\" Davis</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-104\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-104\">[104]</a></sup> The Celtics then traded <a title=\"Ryan Gomes\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ryan_Gomes\">Ryan Gomes</a>, <a title=\"Gerald Green\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_Green\">Gerald Green</a>, Al Jefferson, <a title=\"Theo Ratliff\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theo_Ratliff\">Theo Ratliff</a>, <a title=\"Sebastian Telfair\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sebastian_Telfair\">Sebastian Telfair</a>, and a first-round draft pick to the Timberwolves in exchange for superstar power forward <a title=\"Kevin Garnett\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Garnett\">Kevin Garnett</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-105\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-105\">[105]</a></sup> These moves created a new \"Big Three\" of Pierce, Allen, and Garnett.</p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tmulti tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner multiimageinner\" style=\"width: 342px; max-width: 342px;\">\r\n<div class=\"trow\">\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 195px; max-width: 195px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 210px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kevin_Garnett_in_Green.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Kevin_Garnett_in_Green.jpg/193px-Kevin_Garnett_in_Green.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Kevin_Garnett_in_Green.jpg/290px-Kevin_Garnett_in_Green.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Kevin_Garnett_in_Green.jpg/386px-Kevin_Garnett_in_Green.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"193\" height=\"211\" data-file-width=\"2469\" data-file-height=\"2694\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 143px; max-width: 143px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 210px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:RayAllen20.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/RayAllen20.jpg/141px-RayAllen20.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/RayAllen20.jpg/212px-RayAllen20.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/RayAllen20.jpg/282px-RayAllen20.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"141\" height=\"210\" data-file-width=\"1767\" data-file-height=\"2626\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"trow\" style=\"display: flex;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Kevin Garnett\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Garnett\">Kevin Garnett</a> and <a title=\"Ray Allen\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Allen\">Ray Allen</a> were key players in the Celtics' 2008 NBA title victory</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>In the 2007&ndash;08 season, Celtics completed the largest single-season turnaround in <a title=\"National Basketball Association\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association\">NBA</a> history. The team went 66&ndash;16 in the regular season, a 42-game improvement over its 2006&ndash;07 record. However, the team struggled in the early rounds of the playoffs, needing seven games to defeat the Atlanta Hawks in the first round and another seven to defeat the Cleveland Cavaliers in the conference semifinals. The Celtics then beat the Detroit Pistons in six games in the Eastern Conference Finals, winning two road games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-106\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-106\">[106]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>For the 11th time in league history, and for the first time since 1987, the Celtics and the Lakers faced off in the NBA Finals.
