The Celtics won Game One at home 98&ndash;88, fueled by strong play by Garnett and Pierce's dramatic comeback from a second-half knee injury. They won Game Two 108&ndash;102 despite nearly blowing a 24-point lead in the fourth quarter. As the series shifted to Los Angeles, the Lakers stifled Pierce and Garnett in Game Three and won 87&ndash;81. However, the Celtics would overcome a 24-point deficit in Game 4 to win 97&ndash;91, making the largest in-game comeback in NBA Finals history. After again blowing a large lead, the Lakers hung on to win Game 5 103&ndash;98, sending the series back to Boston. In Game 6, the Celtics overpowered the Lakers, winning 131&ndash;92 and clinching their 17th NBA title. <a title=\"Paul Pierce\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Pierce\">Paul Pierce</a> was named Finals MVP.<sup id=\"cite_ref-107\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-107\">[107]</a></sup> With the win Celtics set a record for most games a team had ever played in a postseason with 26.<sup id=\"cite_ref-108\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-108\">[108]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The 2008&ndash;09 Celtics started off the season at 27&ndash;2, the then-best starting record in NBA history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-109\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-109\">[109]</a></sup> They also had a franchise-record 19-game streak.<sup id=\"cite_ref-110\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-110\">[110]</a></sup> After the All-Star Break, <a title=\"Kevin Garnett\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Garnett\">Kevin Garnett</a> was injured in a loss against the <a title=\"Utah Jazz\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utah_Jazz\">Utah Jazz</a> and missed the last 25 games of the season. Garnett was eventually shelved for the playoffs. The 2009 Celtics still finished with 62 victories, but their playoff run would end against the Magic in the second round.<sup id=\"cite_ref-111\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-111\">[111]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2009, with the return of Garnett from injury and the additions of <a title=\"Rasheed Wallace\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rasheed_Wallace\">Rasheed Wallace</a> and <a title=\"Marquis Daniels\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marquis_Daniels\">Marquis Daniels</a>, the Celtics started the season 23&ndash;5 and at one point had the best record in the NBA. However, Doc Rivers decided to lessen his aging stars' minutes to keep them fresh for the playoffs. As a result, the Celtics sputtered to an even 27&ndash;27 record the rest of the way and finished the 2009&ndash;10 regular season with a 50&ndash;32 record.<sup id=\"cite_ref-112\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-112\">[112]</a></sup> Despite being the fourth seed in the Eastern Conference, the Celtics managed to make the <a title=\"NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>. Rajon Rondo emerged as a star during postseason play.<sup id=\"cite_ref-113\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-113\">[113]</a></sup> For the 12th time, the Celtics faced the Lakers in the Finals. After taking a 3&ndash;2 lead heading into Los Angeles for Game Six, the Celtics appeared poised to win their 18th title. However, starting center <a title=\"Kendrick Perkins\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kendrick_Perkins\">Kendrick Perkins</a> suffered a severe knee injury early in Game Six,<sup id=\"cite_ref-114\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-114\">[114]</a></sup> and the Celtics went on to lose the series in seven games.</p>\r\n<p>During the 2010 offseason, with Perkins expected to be out until February 2011, the Celtics signed two former All-Star centers, <a title=\"Shaquille O'Neal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaquille_O%27Neal\">Shaquille O'Neal</a> and <a title=\"Jermaine O'Neal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jermaine_O%27Neal\">Jermaine O'Neal</a>. Shaquille O'Neal's presence wound up leading to Perkins' departure: the Celtics were 33&ndash;10 in games Perkins had missed during the year due to injury<sup id=\"cite_ref-may_115-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-may-115\">[115]</a></sup> and had a 19&ndash;3 record in games when O'Neal played over 20&nbsp;minutes.<sup id=\"cite_ref-116\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-116\">[116]</a></sup> Consequently, Perkins was traded to the <a title=\"Oklahoma City Thunder\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oklahoma_City_Thunder\">Oklahoma City Thunder</a> in February, when the Celtics were 41&ndash;14 and led the Eastern Conference despite another rash of injuries. Following the trade, however, they proceeded to win only 15 of their final 27 games. They finished with a 56&ndash;26 record, sliding to the third seed.<sup id=\"cite_ref-may_115-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-may-115\">[115]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-117\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-117\">[117]</a></sup> The 2010&ndash;11 season still provided three landmarks: The Celtics became the second team to reach 3,000 victories, Paul Pierce became the third Celtic to score 20,000 points (the others are Larry Bird and John Havlicek), and Ray Allen broke the NBA record for most career three-pointers. The <a title=\"2011 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_NBA_playoffs\">2011 NBA playoffs</a> started with the Celtics sweeping the New York Knicks 4&ndash;0 in the opening round. In the second round, they were ousted by eventual Eastern Conference champions Miami Heat in five games. Shaquille O'Neal, limited to 12&nbsp;minutes in two games of the second round, retired at the end of the season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-118\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-118\">[118]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Celtics started the <a title=\"2011 NBA lockout\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_NBA_lockout\">lockout-shortened</a> season 0&ndash;3, as Pierce was out with a heel injury. At the All-Star break, the Celtics were below .500 with a 15&ndash;17 record. However, they were one of the hottest teams in the league after the break, going 24&ndash;10 the rest of the year and winning their fifth division title in a row. The Celtics made the playoffs as the fourth seed in the Eastern Conference. In the playoffs, the Celtics faced the <a title=\"Atlanta Hawks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Hawks\">Atlanta Hawks</a> in the first round, beating them in six games led by strong play from Pierce and Garnett. In the conference semifinals, the Celtics defeated the 76ers in seven games. The Celtics faced the Miami Heat in the Eastern Conference Finals, losing in seven games to the eventual NBA champions.</p>\r\n<p>The 2012 off-season started with the Celtics having only six players under contract. While Kevin Garnett was signed to a new contract, Ray Allen signed with the Miami Heat for less money than the Celtics offered; this move brought the five-year \"Big Three\" era to a somewhat acrimonious end. The Celtics finished the season with 41 wins.<sup id=\"cite_ref-119\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-119\">[119]</a></sup> The Celtics trailed the New York Knicks 3&ndash;0 in the first round of the <a title=\"2013 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_NBA_playoffs\">2013 NBA playoffs</a> before losing the series in six games. In Game Six, the Celtics nearly completed a comeback when they went on a 20&ndash;0 run to cut the lead to four.<sup id=\"cite_ref-120\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-120\">[120]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"2013.E2.80.932016:_post-Pierce_era\"></span><span id=\"2013&ndash;2016:_post-Pierce_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">2013&ndash;2016: post-Pierce era</span></h3>\r\n<p>During the off-season, head coach <a title=\"Doc Rivers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doc_Rivers\">Doc Rivers</a> was allowed to terminate his contract. He departed the Celtics to coach the Los Angeles Clippers, and the Celtics received a 2015 unprotected first-round pick as compensation. A few days later, Pierce, Garnett (who waived a no-trade clause), <a title=\"Jason Terry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jason_Terry\">Jason Terry</a>, and <a title=\"D. J. White\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D._J._White\">D. J. White</a>, were traded to the <a title=\"Brooklyn Nets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets\">Brooklyn Nets</a> for <a title=\"Keith Bogans\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keith_Bogans\">Keith Bogans</a>, <a title=\"MarShon Brooks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MarShon_Brooks\">MarShon Brooks</a>, <a title=\"Kris Humphries\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kris_Humphries\">Kris Humphries</a>, <a title=\"Kris Joseph\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kris_Joseph\">Kris Joseph</a>, <a title=\"Gerald Wallace\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_Wallace\">Gerald Wallace</a>, and three future first-round draft picks (2014, 2016, 2018), together with the right to swap 2017 first-round picks with Brooklyn.<sup id=\"cite_ref-121\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-121\">[121]</a></sup> The deal marked the start of a youth movement for the team.<sup id=\"cite_ref-122\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-122\">[122]</a></sup></p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 182px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Brad_Stevens_2017.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Brad_Stevens_2017.jpg/180px-Brad_Stevens_2017.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Brad_Stevens_2017.jpg/270px-Brad_Stevens_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Brad_Stevens_2017.jpg/360px-Brad_Stevens_2017.jpg 2x\" width=\"180\" height=\"184\" data-file-width=\"1698\" data-file-height=\"1736\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 182px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Brad Stevens\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brad_Stevens\">Brad Stevens</a>, former head coach of the Celtics.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>On July 3, 2013, the Celtics announced that <a title=\"Brad Stevens\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brad_Stevens\">Brad Stevens</a>, the head coach of <a title=\"Butler Bulldogs men's basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Butler_Bulldogs_men%27s_basketball\">Butler University</a>, would replace Doc Rivers as head coach.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Stevens2013_123-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-Stevens2013-123\">[123]</a></sup> Halfway through the season, in January, Rajon Rondo made his return and was named the 15th Team Captain in team history, and the team furthered the youth movement by acquiring two draft picks in a three-team trade that sent Jordan Crawford and MarShon Brooks to the Golden State Warriors while the Celtics received the Heat center <a title=\"Joel Anthony\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joel_Anthony\">Joel Anthony</a>. The 2013&ndash;14 season marked the Celtics' first missed playoffs since the \"Big Three\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-124\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-124\">[124]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The next off-season, the Celtics drafted <a title=\"Marcus Smart\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Smart\">Marcus Smart</a> with the 6th overall pick and <a title=\"James Young (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Young_(basketball)\">James Young</a> with the 17th overall pick in the <a title=\"2014 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_NBA_draft\">2014 NBA draft</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-125\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-125\">[125]</a></sup> and signed <a title=\"Evan Turner\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evan_Turner\">Evan Turner</a>. The 2014&ndash;15 season had several roster moves, the most prominent being Rondo and rookie <a title=\"Dwight Powell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwight_Powell\">Dwight Powell</a> traded to the Dallas Mavericks for center <a title=\"Brandan Wright\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brandan_Wright\">Brandan Wright</a>, forward <a title=\"Jae Crowder\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jae_Crowder\">Jae Crowder</a>, veteran point guard <a title=\"Jameer Nelson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jameer_Nelson\">Jameer Nelson</a>, and future picks.<sup id=\"cite_ref-126\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-126\">[126]</a></sup> A total of 22 players spent time with the Celtics,<sup id=\"cite_ref-127\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-127\">[127]</a></sup> leading scorer and rebounder Sullinger suffered a season-ending left metatarsal stress fracture,<sup id=\"cite_ref-128\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-128\">[128]</a></sup> and the team was only tenth in the East with 28 games remaining.<sup id=\"cite_ref-129\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-129\">[129]</a></sup> However, midseason acquisition <a title=\"Isaiah Thomas (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaiah_Thomas_(basketball)\">Isaiah Thomas</a> helped the team win 22 of their last 34 games, finishing the season with a 40&ndash;42 record, enough for the seventh seed in the <a title=\"2015 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_NBA_playoffs\">Eastern Conference Playoffs</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-130\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-130\">[130]</a></sup> The Celtics were swept by the second seeded Cleveland Cavaliers in the first round.</p>\r\n<p>In the <a title=\"2015 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_NBA_draft\">2015 NBA draft</a> Boston selected <a title=\"Terry Rozier\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terry_Rozier\">Terry Rozier</a>, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"R.J. Hunter\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/R.J._Hunter\">R.J. Hunter</a>, <a title=\"Jordan Mickey\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_Mickey\">Jordan Mickey</a>, and <a title=\"Marcus Thornton (basketball, born 1993)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Thornton_(basketball,_born_1993)\">Marcus Thornton</a> with the 16th, 28th, 33rd, and 45th selections respectively. During the off-season, the Celtics signed forward <a title=\"Amir Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amir_Johnson\">Amir Johnson</a> and traded <a title=\"Gerald Wallace\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_Wallace\">Gerald Wallace</a> and <a title=\"Chris Babb\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Babb\">Chris Babb</a> in exchange for Warriors forward David Lee. The Celtics finished the 2015&ndash;16 NBA season with a 48&ndash;34 record, earning the fifth seed in the Eastern Conference. They played the fourth seed Atlanta Hawks in the first round of the playoffs. After leading by 3 points in the fourth quarter of Game 1, guard Avery Bradley went down with a hamstring injury, making him sit out for the rest of the series. The Celtics lost the series 4&ndash;2 to the Hawks, ending their season.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"2016.E2.80.93present:_.22The_Jays.22:_Jaylen_Brown_and_Jayson_Tatum_era\"></span><span id=\"2016&ndash;present:_&quot;The_Jays&quot;:_Jaylen_Brown_and_Jayson_Tatum_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">2016&ndash;present: \"The Jays\": Jaylen Brown and Jayson Tatum era</span></h3>\r\n<table class=\"box-Overly_detailed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-overly_detailed\" role=\"presentation\">\r\n<tbody>\r\n<tr>\r\n<td class=\"mbox-image\">\r\n<div class=\"mbox-image-div\"><img class=\"mbox-text\">\r\n<div class=\"mbox-text-span\">This section <strong>may contain an excessive amount of intricate detail that may interest only a particular audience</strong>. message</a></small>)</em></span></div>\r\n</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n</tbody>\r\n</table>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tmulti tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner multiimageinner\" style=\"width: 342px; max-width: 342px;\">\r\n<div class=\"trow\">\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 163px; max-width: 163px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 272px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jaylen_Brown_2022.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Jaylen_Brown_2022.jpg/161px-Jaylen_Brown_2022.jpg\" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Jaylen_Brown_2022.jpg/322px-Jaylen_Brown_2022.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"161\" height=\"273\" data-file-width=\"1497\" data-file-height=\"2535\"></a></div>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Jaylen Brown\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaylen_Brown\">Jaylen Brown</a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 175px; max-width: 175px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 272px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jayson_Tatum_(51839569977)_(cropped).jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Jayson_Tatum_%2851839569977%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/173px-Jayson_Tatum_%2851839569977%29_%28cropped%29.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Jayson_Tatum_%2851839569977%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/260px-Jayson_Tatum_%2851839569977%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Jayson_Tatum_%2851839569977%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/346px-Jayson_Tatum_%2851839569977%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"173\" height=\"273\" data-file-width=\"1450\" data-file-height=\"2287\"></a></div>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Jayson Tatum\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jayson_Tatum\">Jayson Tatum</a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>In the <a title=\"2016 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_NBA_draft\">2016 NBA draft</a>, the Celtics selected <a title=\"Jaylen Brown\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaylen_Brown\">Jaylen Brown</a> with the third pick. At the time, he was a tenacious defender with raw athletic ability who is now an elite offensive threat. On July 8, 2016, the Celtics signed four-time All-Star <a title=\"Al Horford\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Horford\">Al Horford</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-131\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-131\">[131]</a></sup> The Celtics finished the <a title=\"2016&ndash;17 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_NBA_season\">2016&ndash;17 season</a> with a 53&ndash;29 record and clinched the top seed in the Eastern Conference.<sup id=\"cite_ref-132\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-132\">[132]</a></sup> After a hip injury ended Thomas' impressive playoff run in game 2 of the Eastern Conference Finals,<sup id=\"cite_ref-133\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-133\">[133]</a></sup> the Celtics eventually lost to the Cavaliers in five games. For the <a title=\"2017 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_NBA_draft\">2017 NBA draft</a>, the Celtics won the draft lottery, earning them the first pick.<sup id=\"cite_ref-2017_draft_lottery_134-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-2017_draft_lottery-134\">[note 1]</a></sup> They were projected to select freshman guard <a title=\"Markelle Fultz\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markelle_Fultz\">Markelle Fultz</a>, but the pick was subsequently traded to the Philadelphia 76ers in exchange for the third pick in the 2017 draft and future picks.<sup id=\"cite_ref-135\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-135\">[134]</a></sup> The 76ers would go on to draft Fultz, while the Celtics used the third pick to select freshman forward <a title=\"Jayson Tatum\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jayson_Tatum\">Jayson Tatum</a>. <a title=\"Semi Ojeleye\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi_Ojeleye\">Semi Ojeleye</a>, <a title=\"Kadeem Allen\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kadeem_Allen\">Kadeem Allen</a>, and <a title=\"Jabari Bird\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jabari_Bird\">Jabari Bird</a> were selected with the 37th, 53rd, and 56th selections, respectively, in the second round.<sup id=\"cite_ref-136\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-136\">[135]</a></sup> At the start of the off-season, the team signed Tatum and <a title=\"Ante Žižić\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ante_%C5%BDi%C5%BEi%C4%87\">Ante Žižić</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-137\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-137\">[136]</a></sup> among others, with the biggest acquisition being the signing of <a title=\"Gordon Hayward\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gordon_Hayward\">Gordon Hayward</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-138\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-138\">[137]</a></sup> On August 22, 2017, the Celtics agreed to a deal that sent <a title=\"Isaiah Thomas (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaiah_Thomas_(basketball)\">Isaiah Thomas</a>, <a title=\"Jae Crowder\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jae_Crowder\">Jae Crowder</a>, Žižić, and the Brooklyn Nets' 2018 first round draft pick to the Cleveland Cavaliers in exchange for <a title=\"Kyrie Irving\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyrie_Irving\">Kyrie Irving</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-139\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-139\">[138]</a></sup> An additional draft pick (Celtics' 2020 second round) was later added to the package from the Celtics to the Cavaliers after doctors revealed that Thomas's injury was more significant than initially anticipated.<sup id=\"cite_ref-140\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-140\">[139]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>By the end of the off-season, only four Celtics' players remained from the <a title=\"2016&ndash;17 Boston Celtics season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Boston_Celtics_season\">2016&ndash;17 team</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-141\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-141\">[140]</a></sup> with <a title=\"Marcus Smart\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Smart\">Marcus Smart</a> being the longest-tenured Celtic from the <a title=\"2014 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_NBA_draft\">2014 NBA draft</a>. On the team's opening night game in the first quarter against the Cavaliers, Hayward suffered a fractured tibia and dislocated ankle in his left leg,<sup id=\"cite_ref-142\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-142\">[141]</a></sup> causing him to be ruled out for the rest of the regular season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-143\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-143\">[142]</a></sup> Despite the loss, the Celtics went on a <a title=\"List of National Basketball Association longest winning streaks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_National_Basketball_Association_longest_winning_streaks\">16-game winning streak</a>, which also went down as the fourth-longest winning streak in the teams' history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-144\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-144\">[143]</a></sup> The streak started with a 102&ndash;92 victory over the Philadelphia 76ers on October 20 and ended on November 22 to the hands of the Miami Heat with a 104&ndash;98 loss. The Celtics finished the year with a 55&ndash;27 record, good enough for second place in the Eastern Conference. In the playoffs, they defeated the Milwaukee Bucks in the First Round in seven games, and continued the feat in the Conference Semifinals by defeating the Philadelphia 76ers in five games before losing to the Cleveland Cavaliers in seven games in the Conference Finals.</p>\r\n<p>The Celtics finished the <a title=\"2018&ndash;19 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_NBA_season\">2018&ndash;19 season</a> with a 49&ndash;33 record. Analysts started questioning team's performance and chances for the championship when the Celtics had a 10&ndash;10 record after the first 20 games on November 24, 2018.<sup id=\"cite_ref-145\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-145\">[144]</a></sup> The Celtics then won the next eight games improving their record to 18&ndash;10.<sup id=\"cite_ref-146\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-146\">[145]</a></sup> During the eight-game win streak, the Celtics defeated the Cleveland Cavaliers 128&ndash;95, the New York Knicks 128&ndash;100, and also defeated the Chicago Bulls by 56 points (133&ndash;77), setting a record for the largest margin in a victory in franchise history, while also tying the record for largest victory margin by an away team.<sup id=\"cite_ref-147\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-147\">[146]</a></sup> On February 9, 2019, the Celtics lost 129&ndash;128 to the Los Angeles Lakers after former Celtic <a title=\"Rajon Rondo\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajon_Rondo\">Rajon Rondo</a> hit the first game-winning shot in his NBA career.<sup id=\"cite_ref-148\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-148\">[147]</a></sup> The Celtics finished the regular season place fourth in the Eastern Conference. During an April 7 game, <a title=\"Marcus Smart\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Smart\">Marcus Smart</a> injured his hip and was ruled out for the rest of the regular season and the first round of the playoffs.<sup id=\"cite_ref-149\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-149\">[148]</a></sup> In the <a title=\"2019 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_NBA_playoffs\">2019 playoffs</a>, the Celtics swept the Indiana Pacers in the first round, and then lost to the Milwaukee Bucks in five games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-150\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-150\">[149]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Celtics held four picks in the <a title=\"2019 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_NBA_draft\">2019 NBA draft</a>. Following a series of transactions, the team landed <a title=\"Romeo Langford\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romeo_Langford\">Romeo Langford</a> with the 14th pick and also added <a title=\"Grant Williams (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grant_Williams_(basketball)\">Grant Williams</a>, <a title=\"Carsen Edwards\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carsen_Edwards\">Carsen Edwards</a>, and <a title=\"Tremont Waters\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tremont_Waters\">Tremont Waters</a> (2020 G-league Rookie of the year).<sup id=\"cite_ref-151\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-151\">[150]</a></sup> During the 2019 offseason, Irving and Horford signed with the Brooklyn Nets and Philadelphia 76ers, respectively. On June 30, 2019, the Celtics and point guard <a title=\"Kemba Walker\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kemba_Walker\">Kemba Walker</a> agreed to a four-year maximum contract worth $141 million. On July 6, 2019, the Celtics officially acquired Walker in a sign and trade with the Charlotte Hornets; the Celtics sent guard Terry Rozier and a protected 2020 second-round draft pick to Charlotte in exchange for Walker and a 2020 second-round draft pick.<sup id=\"cite_ref-152\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-152\">[151]</a></sup> On July 1, 2019, the Celtics agreed to a two-year contract with center <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Enes Kanter\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enes_Kanter\">Enes Kanter</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-153\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-153\">[152]</a></sup> On July 25, 2019, the Celtics agreed to a rookie contract with 7&nbsp;ft 5&nbsp;in (2.26&nbsp;m) center <a title=\"Tacko Fall\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tacko_Fall\">Tacko Fall</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-154\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-154\">[153]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-155\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-155\">[154]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-156\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-156\">[155]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Following the <a title=\"Suspension of the 2019&ndash;20 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suspension_of_the_2019%E2%80%9320_NBA_season\">suspension of the 2019&ndash;20 NBA season</a>, the Celtics were one of the 22 teams invited to the <a title=\"2020 NBA Bubble\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_NBA_Bubble\">NBA Bubble</a> to participate in the final 8 games of the regular season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-157\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-157\">[156]</a></sup> In the <a title=\"2020 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_NBA_playoffs\">2020 playoffs</a>, the Celtics swept the Philadelphia 76ers in the first round, beat the Toronto Raptors in a seven-game series, and fell to the Miami Heat in the Eastern Conference Finals in six games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-158\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-158\">[157]</a></sup> Boston struggled with injuries in the 2020&ndash;21 season, with Walker, Tatum and Brown all missing games at different points in the season due to injury and COVID-19. The injury of Brown was particularly impactful as he would miss the playoffs. Boston could not automatically qualify for the playoffs and were sent to the play-in tournament where they defeated the Washington Wizards 119&ndash;100. In the playoffs they lost to the Brooklyn Nets in five games. With a highlight being Tatum's 50 point game in a Game 3 victory. After Game 4, a Celtics fan threw a plastic water bottle at Irving.<sup id=\"cite_ref-159\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-159\">[158]</a></sup> When asked about it after the game, Irving talked about the \"underlying racism\" that leads to fans treating athletes like they are in a \"human zoo\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-160\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-160\">[159]</a></sup> This was not the former Celtics' first time speaking out against racism in Boston. Before the playoff series, he was asked whether or not he experienced racism while in the TD Garden and responded: \"I'm not the only one that could attest to this, but it's just, you know &mdash; it is what it is.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-161\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-161\">[160]</a></sup> Irving was not alone in sharing this sentiment. After the incident, several players shared their experience, including Celtics center <a title=\"Tristan Thompson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tristan_Thompson\">Tristan Thompson</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-162\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-162\">[161]</a></sup> and guard <a title=\"Marcus Smart\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Smart\">Marcus Smart</a>, who wrote about an encounter with a Celtics fan who had called him a slur in <em><a title=\"The Players' Tribune\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Players%27_Tribune\">The Players' Tribune</a></em> the summer before the season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-163\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-163\">[162]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>On June 2, 2021, the Celtics named head coach Brad Stevens as president of basketball operations replacing <a title=\"Danny Ainge\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danny_Ainge\">Danny Ainge</a> after he announced his retirement.<sup id=\"cite_ref-164\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-164\">[163]</a></sup> On June 18, Stevens made his first transaction in his new position trading away <a title=\"Kemba Walker\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kemba_Walker\">Kemba Walker</a>, the 16th pick in the <a title=\"2021 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_NBA_draft\">2021 NBA draft</a>, and a 2025 second-round pick in exchange for Horford, <a title=\"Moses Brown (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moses_Brown_(basketball)\">Moses Brown</a>, and a 2023 second-round pick.<sup id=\"cite_ref-165\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-165\">[164]</a></sup> The deal gave the Celtics a bit more financial flexibility with Horford due about $20 million less than Walker over the next two years. The Celtics also improved their depth in the frontcourt by adding Horford and <a title=\"Moses Brown (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moses_Brown_(basketball)\">Moses Brown</a>, who recorded 21 points and 23 rebounds, which included 19 rebounds in the first half, in a March 27 game between the Celtics and the Thunder.<sup id=\"cite_ref-166\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-166\">[165]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-167\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-167\">[166]</a></sup> On June 23, 2021, it was reported that Stevens had made the decision to hire <a title=\"Ime Udoka\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ime_Udoka\">Ime Udoka</a> as his own replacement as head coach of the Celtics.<sup id=\"cite_ref-168\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-168\">[167]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-169\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-169\">[168]</a></sup> Tatum made his third All-Star appearance off the bench at the <a title=\"2022 NBA All-Star Game\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_NBA_All-Star_Game\">2022 NBA All-Star Game</a> in Cleveland.</p>\r\n<p>In April 2022, the Celtics qualified for the <a title=\"2022 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_NBA_playoffs\">2022 NBA playoffs</a> as the second seed in the Eastern Conference, having a 51&ndash;31 record and swept the Brooklyn Nets in the first round of the postseason.<sup id=\"cite_ref-170\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-170\">[169]</a></sup> They next faced the Milwaukee Bucks in the Eastern Conference Semifinals and the Miami Heat in the Eastern Conference Finals, defeating both teams in seven-game series, earning the Celtics their first Finals appearance since 2010. The Celtics took a 2&ndash;1 series lead, but lost the next three games to lose to the Golden State Warriors 4&ndash;2.<sup id=\"cite_ref-171\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-171\">[170]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Rivalries\" class=\"mw-headline\">Rivalries</span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Los_Angeles_Lakers\" class=\"mw-headline\">Los Angeles Lakers</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"Celtics&ndash;Lakers rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtics%E2%80%93Lakers_rivalry\">Celtics&ndash;Lakers rivalry</a></div>\r\n<p>The rivalry between the Boston Celtics and <a title=\"Los Angeles Lakers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers\">Los Angeles Lakers</a> involves the two most storied franchises in NBA history. It has been called the NBA's best rivalry.<sup id=\"cite_ref-172\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-172\">[171]</a></sup> The two teams have met a record twelve times in the <a title=\"NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>, starting with their first Finals meeting in <a title=\"1959 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1959_NBA_Finals\">1959</a>. They would go on to dominate the league in the 1960s and the 1980s, facing each other six times in the 1960s, three times in the 1980s, in 2008, and in 2010.</p>\r\n<p>The Celtics have won the first eight finals meetings, while the Lakers won three of last four.</p>\r\n<p>The rivalry had been less intense since the retirements of <a title=\"Magic Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_Johnson\">Magic Johnson</a> and Larry Bird in the early 1990s, but in 2008 it was renewed as the Celtics and Lakers met in the Finals for the first time since 1987, with the Celtics winning the series in six games. They faced off once again in the <a title=\"2010 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_NBA_Finals\">2010 NBA Finals</a> which the Lakers won in seven games. The two teams are tied for the highest number of championships (17); together, the 34 championships account for almost half of the <a title=\"List of NBA champions\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_NBA_champions\">74 championships</a> in NBA history.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Atlanta_Hawks\" class=\"mw-headline\">Atlanta Hawks</span></h3>\r\n<p>The Celtics&ndash;<a title=\"Atlanta Hawks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Hawks\">Hawks</a> rivalry is a <a title=\"List of sports rivalries\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_sports_rivalries\">rivalry</a> in the <a title=\"Eastern Conference (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Conference_(NBA)\">Eastern Conference</a> of the <a title=\"National Basketball Association\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association\">National Basketball Association</a> that has lasted for over five decades, although the two teams have played each other since the 1949&ndash;50 season, when the then-<a title=\"Quad Cities\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quad_Cities\">Tri-Cities</a> Blackhawks joined the NBA as part of the <a title=\"National Basketball League (United States)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_League_(United_States)\">National Basketball League</a> and the <a title=\"Basketball Association of America\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball_Association_of_America\">Basketball Association of America</a> merger. However, the Blackhawks could not field a truly competitive team until they moved to <a title=\"St. Louis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis\">St. Louis</a> as the St. Louis Hawks after a four-year stopover at <a title=\"Milwaukee\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milwaukee\">Milwaukee</a>. The two teams have faced each other eleven times in the NBA Playoffs, four times in the <a title=\"NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>, with the Celtics winning ten of twelve series against the Hawks, including three out of four NBA Finals.<sup id=\"cite_ref-celticsrecap1950s_173-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-celticsrecap1950s-173\">[172]</a></sup> While the Hawks have only defeated the Celtics twice out of eleven series in the NBA Playoffs, they still often managed to make their series with the Celtics memorable. The rivalry intensified in 2016 with Hawks All-Star Center <a title=\"Al Horford\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Horford\">Al Horford</a> spurning the team and joining the Celtics.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Brooklyn_Nets\" class=\"mw-headline\">Brooklyn Nets</span></h3>\r\n<p>The Boston Celtics were once rivals of the <a title=\"Brooklyn Nets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets\">New Jersey Nets</a> during the early 2000s due to their respective locations and their burgeoning stars. The Nets were led by <a title=\"Jason Kidd\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jason_Kidd\">Jason Kidd</a> and <a title=\"Kenyon Martin\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kenyon_Martin\">Kenyon Martin</a>, while the Celtics were experiencing newfound success behind Paul Pierce and Antoine Walker. The rivalry began to heat up in the 2002 Eastern Conference Finals, which was preceded by trash-talking from the Celtics<sup id=\"cite_ref-174\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-174\">[173]</a></sup> who claimed Martin was a \"fake\" tough guy. Things progressed as the series started, and on-court tensions seemed to spill into the stands. Celtics' fans berated Kidd and his family with chants of \"Wife Beater!\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-175\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-175\">[174]</a></sup> in response to Kidd's 2001 domestic abuse charge. When asked about the fan barbs being traded, <a title=\"Kenyon Martin\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kenyon_Martin\">Kenyon Martin</a> stated, \"Our fans hate them, their fans hate us.\" <a title=\"Bill Walton\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Walton\">Bill Walton</a> said at the time that Nets-Celtics was the \"beginning of the next great NBA rivalry\" during the Eastern Conference Finals in 2002 with the Nets advancing to the NBA Finals, though New Jersey would go on to sweep Boston in the 2003 playoffs. In 2012, the year the Nets returned to New York in the borough of Brooklyn, there were indications that the rivalry might be rekindled when an altercation occurred on the court on November 28, resulting in the ejection of <a title=\"Rajon Rondo\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajon_Rondo\">Rajon Rondo</a>, Gerald Wallace, and Kris Humphries. Rondo was suspended for two games in the aftermath, while Wallace and <a title=\"Kevin Garnett\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Garnett\">Kevin Garnett</a> were fined.<sup id=\"cite_ref-176\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-176\">[175]</a></sup> The story was revisited on December 25, when Wallace grabbed Garnett's shorts and the two had to be broken up by referees and players alike. However, the rivalry between the Nets and the Celtics appeared significantly cooled off by the June 2013 blockbuster trade that dealt Celtics stars Garnett and <a title=\"Paul Pierce\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Pierce\">Paul Pierce</a> to the Nets in exchange for Wallace, Humphries, and others. This move was billed as a merger of the two <a title=\"Atlantic Division (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Division_(NBA)\">Atlantic Division</a> teams.<sup id=\"cite_ref-177\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-177\">[176]</a></sup> Celtics announcer <a title=\"Sean Grande\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sean_Grande\">Sean Grande</a> said \"It's almost as if you found a great home for these guys. You couldn't have found a better place. These guys will be in the New York market, they'll be on a competitive team, they'll stay on national TV. It's funny, because the enemy of my enemy is my friend. So with Celtics fans feeling the way they do about the Heat, feeling the way they do about the Knicks, the Nets are going to become almost the second [Boston] team now.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-178\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-178\">[177]</a></sup> The trade would end up crippling the Nets who posted a record of 151&ndash;259 following the trade including three consecutive seasons with fewer than 30 wins from 2016 to 2018. Brooklyn would win just one playoff series with Garnett and Pierce, neither of whom were with the team by the close of the <a title=\"2014&ndash;15 Brooklyn Nets season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Brooklyn_Nets_season\">2014&ndash;2015 season</a>. The Celtics would use Brooklyn's draft picks to acquire <a title=\"Jaylen Brown\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaylen_Brown\">Jaylen Brown</a> and <a title=\"Jayson Tatum\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jayson_Tatum\">Jayson Tatum</a> through the draft in <a title=\"2016 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_NBA_draft\">2016</a> and <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"2017 NBA Draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_NBA_Draft\">2017</a> respectively and <a title=\"Kyrie Irving\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyrie_Irving\">Kyrie Irving</a> via trade, en route to consecutive appearances in the Eastern Conference Finals in <a title=\"2017 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_NBA_playoffs\">2017</a> and <a title=\"2018 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_NBA_playoffs\">2018</a>. Irving then left to the Nets in the 2019 <a title=\"2019&ndash;20 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_NBA_season#Free_agency\">Free Agency</a>. The Celtics would meet the Nets in the following two playoffs in the Eastern Conference first round, with the Nets beating the Celtics 4-1 in the 2021, followed by the Celtics beating the Nets 4-0 in 2022.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Detroit_Pistons\" class=\"mw-headline\">Detroit Pistons</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"Celtics&ndash;Pistons rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtics%E2%80%93Pistons_rivalry\">Celtics&ndash;Pistons rivalry</a></div>\r\n<p>The rivalry between the Celtics and the <a title=\"Detroit Pistons\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Detroit_Pistons\">Detroit Pistons</a> peaked in the 1980s, featuring players such as Larry Bird, Kevin McHale, Robert Parish, <a title=\"Isiah Thomas\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isiah_Thomas\">Isiah Thomas</a>, <a title=\"Bill Laimbeer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Laimbeer\">Bill Laimbeer</a>, <a title=\"Dennis Rodman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dennis_Rodman\">Dennis Rodman</a>, and <a title=\"Joe Dumars\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Dumars\">Joe Dumars</a>. These teams met in the <a title=\"NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_playoffs\">NBA playoffs</a> five times in 7 seasons from 1985 to 1991, with the Celtics winning in 1985 and 1987, and the Pistons coming out on top en route to back-to-back Finals appearances in <a title=\"1988 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_NBA_Finals\">1988</a> and their championship seasons of <a title=\"1989 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989_NBA_Finals\">1989</a> and <a title=\"1990 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990_NBA_Finals\">1990</a>. Led by <a title=\"Paul Pierce\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Pierce\">Paul Pierce</a>, <a title=\"Kevin Garnett\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Garnett\">Kevin Garnett</a> and <a title=\"Ray Allen\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Allen\">Ray Allen</a> in the 2008 <a title=\"NBA Conference Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Conference_Finals\">Eastern Conference Finals</a> the Celtics defeated the Pistons in 6 games to advance to the NBA Finals where they went on to beat the Lakers also in 6 games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-179\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-179\">[178]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"New_York_Knicks\" class=\"mw-headline\">New York Knicks</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"Celtics&ndash;Knicks rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtics%E2%80%93Knicks_rivalry\">Celtics&ndash;Knicks rivalry</a></div>\r\n<p>The rivalry between the Celtics and the <a title=\"New York Knicks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Knicks\">New York Knicks</a> stems from the location of the teams, both of which are in the NBA's Atlantic division. It is one of many rivalries between Boston and New York teams. Boston and New York are also the only two original NBA franchises that have remained in the same city for the duration of their existence. The teams have played 512 games against each other during the regular season, with the Celtics winning 276 times. The two teams have also faced each other 61 times during the playoffs, with the Celtics winning 34 times.<sup id=\"cite_ref-180\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-180\">[179]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Philadelphia_76ers\" class=\"mw-headline\">Philadelphia 76ers</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"76ers&ndash;Celtics rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/76ers%E2%80%93Celtics_rivalry\">76ers&ndash;Celtics rivalry</a></div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 202px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wilt_Chamberlain_Bill_Russell_2.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Wilt_Chamberlain_Bill_Russell_2.jpg/200px-Wilt_Chamberlain_Bill_Russell_2.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Wilt_Chamberlain_Bill_Russell_2.jpg/300px-Wilt_Chamberlain_Bill_Russell_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Wilt_Chamberlain_Bill_Russell_2.jpg/400px-Wilt_Chamberlain_Bill_Russell_2.jpg 2x\" width=\"200\" height=\"271\" data-file-width=\"931\" data-file-height=\"1263\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 202px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Wilt Chamberlain\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilt_Chamberlain\">Wilt Chamberlain</a> of the Philadelphia 76ers being defended by Celtics' center <a title=\"Bill Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Russell\">Bill Russell</a> in 1966</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The Celtics and the <a title=\"Philadelphia 76ers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philadelphia_76ers\">Philadelphia 76ers</a> are the two teams who have the most meetings in the <a title=\"NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_playoffs\">NBA playoffs</a>, playing each other in 22 series, of which the Celtics have won 15.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Most_frequent_playoff_matchups_181-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-Most_frequent_playoff_matchups-181\">[180]</a></sup> The 76ers are considered the Celtics' biggest rival in the Eastern Conference. The rivalry reached its peak when players Bill Russell and <a title=\"Wilt Chamberlain\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilt_Chamberlain\">Wilt Chamberlain</a> of the 76ers played each other from 1965 to 1968. Their play would result in the Celtics not winning every NBA Finals series in the 1960s when the 76ers won in 1967.<sup id=\"cite_ref-182\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-182\">[181]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Washington_Wizards\" class=\"mw-headline\">Washington Wizards</span></h3>\r\n<p>One of the most recent and unexpected rivalries that has been created between the Celtics is with the <a title=\"Washington Wizards\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Wizards\">Washington Wizards</a>. Although both teams had engaged in a fight in <a title=\"1984 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984_NBA_playoffs\">1984</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-183\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-183\">[182]</a></sup> the rivalry intensified during the 2015&ndash;16 season in a January regular-season game after <a title=\"Jae Crowder\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jae_Crowder\">Jae Crowder</a> was given a technical foul. Crowder then began to exchange words with then Wizards coach <a title=\"Randy Wittman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Randy_Wittman\">Randy Wittman</a>. It began to escalate that off-season when the Celtics were trying to sign <a title=\"Al Horford\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Horford\">Al Horford</a>. It was publicly reported that Jae Crowder emphasized that the Celtics beat the Wizards in all of their meetings that season and should sign with them rather than Washington. In their first meeting of the 2016&ndash;17 season, Wall hit <a title=\"Marcus Smart\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Smart\">Marcus Smart</a> in the back-court when they were up by 20 late in the 4th quarter. Wall was hit with a Flagrant 2 foul and was promptly ejected. Smart immediately got back up and began to scuffle with Wall. Their words continued even after being separated with Wall telling Smart to meet him out back after the game. No incident was reported between the two following the game. In their next meeting, the Celtics won 117&ndash;108. However, after the game Wall and Crowder exchanged words in front of the Wizards bench. Crowder ended up trying to jab his finger at Wall's nose and Wall tried to fight back with a slap. Teammates and coaches from both sides had to step in and separate the two teams but the players continued to yell while entering their respective locker rooms. Police officers had to be on guard between the two locker rooms to ensure no further confrontation. <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Otto Porter\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otto_Porter\">Otto Porter</a> is quoted as calling the Celtics as dirty. <a title=\"Isaiah Thomas (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaiah_Thomas_(basketball)\">Isaiah Thomas</a> replied \"If playing hard is dirty, then I guess we are a dirty team.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-184\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-184\">[183]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In their next game in January, the Wizards wore all black to enter the game. The notion was that it is similar to the attire of a funeral. Their decision worked as they defeated the Celtics 123&ndash;108. The two teams would go on to meet in the Conference Semifinals in the 2017 Playoffs. In Game 1, <a title=\"Markieff Morris\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markieff_Morris\">Markieff Morris</a> landed on Horford's ankle after shooting a jumpshot. Morris sprained his ankle and had to miss the rest of the game which was a 123&ndash;111 loss. Morris believed that Horford did this intentionally. In Game 2, Morris retaliated by grabbing Horford by the waist and pushed him into the seats.<sup id=\"cite_ref-185\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-185\">[184]</a></sup> In Game 3, <a title=\"Kelly Olynyk\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelly_Olynyk\">Kelly Olynyk</a> set a hard screen on <a title=\"Kelly Oubre Jr.\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelly_Oubre_Jr.\">Kelly Oubre</a>. Olynyk's shoulder hit Oubre in the chin causing him to drop to the floor. Oubre angrily rose and pushed Olynyk down onto the floor. Oubre was then assessed a flagrant 2 foul and was ejected while also being suspended for Game 4.<sup id=\"cite_ref-186\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-186\">[185]</a></sup> No significant altercations erupted in the rest of the seven-game series in which the Celtics would go on to win. The rivalry has since dissipated as the Celtics have retooled their roster but their match-ups are still seen as significant as they played on Christmas in 2017.</p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Season-by-season_record\" class=\"mw-headline\">Season-by-season record</span></h2>\r\n<p><em>List of the last five seasons completed by the Celtics. For the full season-by-season history, see <a title=\"List of Boston Celtics seasons\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Boston_Celtics_seasons\">List of Boston Celtics seasons</a>.</em></p>\r\n<p><em><strong>Note:</strong> GP = Games played, W = Wins, L = Losses, W&ndash;L% = Winning percentage</em></p>\r\n<table class=\"wikitable\">\r\n<tbody>\r\n<tr Conference Finals, 3&ndash;4 (<a title=\"Miami Heat\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miami_Heat\">Heat</a>)</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n</tbody>\r\n</table>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Records.2C_retired_numbers.2C_and_awards\"></span><span id=\"Records,_retired_numbers,_and_awards\" class=\"mw-headline\">Records, retired numbers, and awards</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"Boston Celtics accomplishments and records\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics_accomplishments_and_records\">Boston Celtics accomplishments and records</a></div>\r\n<p>The Celtics are tied with the Los Angeles Lakers for an NBA record 17 championships. Celtics have won 8 in a row and 11 championships in 13 years. They also have 56 playoff appearances. The <a title=\"Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame\">Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame</a> have 48 enshrinees who contributed to the Celtics,<sup id=\"cite_ref-187\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-187\">[186]</a></sup> and the franchise has <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Retired numbers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retired_numbers\">retired</a> 23 <a title=\"Number (sports)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number_(sports)\">jersey numbers</a>, more than any other American sports team.<sup id=\"cite_ref-188\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-188\">[187]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"FIBA_Hall_of_Fame\" class=\"mw-headline\">FIBA Hall of Fame</span></h3>\r\n<p><a title=\"FIBA\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIBA\">FIBA</a>, the body which governs international basketball, has selected two players associated with the Celtics to the <a title=\"FIBA Hall of Fame\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIBA_Hall_of_Fame\">FIBA Hall of Fame</a> for contributions to international basketball.</p>\r\n<table class=\"wikitable\" style=\"text-align: href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lipofsky-Boston-Garden.jpg\"><img href=\"http://www.nba.com/celtics/roster/\" rel=\"nofollow\">Roster</a> <br>Last transaction: June 23, 2023</p>\r\n</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n</tbody>\r\n</table>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Retained_draft_rights\" class=\"mw-headline\">Retained draft rights</span></h3>\r\n<p>The Celtics hold the draft rights to the following unsigned draft picks who have been playing outside the NBA. A drafted player is ostensibly either an international draftee or a college draftee who is not signed by the team that drafted him, is allowed to sign with any non-NBA teams. In this case, the team retains the player's draft rights in the NBA until one year after the player's contract with the non-NBA team ends.<sup id=\"cite_ref-189\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-189\">[188]</a></sup> This list includes draft rights that were acquired from trades with other teams.</p>\r\n<table class=\"wikitable
