both;\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Coaches\" class=\"mw-headline\">Coaches</span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Head_coaches\" class=\"mw-headline\">Head coaches</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"List of Boston Celtics head coaches\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Boston_Celtics_head_coaches\">List of Boston Celtics head coaches</a></div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 207px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Auerbach_Lipofsky.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Auerbach_Lipofsky.jpg\" width=\"205\" height=\"250\" data-file-width=\"205\" data-file-height=\"250\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 207px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Red Auerbach\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Auerbach\">Red Auerbach</a> coached the Boston Celtics to 9 NBA titles, with eight straight between 1959 and 1966.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>There have been 18 head coaches in Celtics' history. <a title=\"Red Auerbach\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Auerbach\">Red Auerbach</a> is the most successful franchise's head coach having won 9 NBA championships with the team. Celtics' legend <a title=\"Bill Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Russell\">Bill Russell</a> took coaching duties from Auerbach and led them to 2 NBA championships while playing and coaching at the same time. The other two coaches that won 2 NBA titles with the team are <a title=\"Tom Heinsohn\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Heinsohn\">Tom Heinsohn</a> and <a title=\"K. C. Jones\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K._C._Jones\">K. C. Jones</a>. Both <a title=\"Bill Fitch\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Fitch\">Bill Fitch</a> and <a title=\"Doc Rivers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doc_Rivers\">Doc Rivers</a> led the Celtics to 1 NBA championship the latter being the most recent coach to do so. <a title=\"Joe Mazzulla\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Mazzulla\">Joe Mazzulla</a> is the team's current head coach.<sup id=\"cite_ref-211\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-211\">[210]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Logos_and_uniforms\" class=\"mw-headline\">Logos and uniforms</span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Logos\" class=\"mw-headline\">Logos</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 152px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CelticsWordmark.svg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/CelticsWordmark.svg/150px-CelticsWordmark.svg.png\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/CelticsWordmark.svg/225px-CelticsWordmark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/CelticsWordmark.svg/300px-CelticsWordmark.svg.png 2x\" width=\"150\" height=\"74\" data-file-width=\"700\" data-file-height=\"344\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tleft\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 152px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">The Celtics' wordmark, used since the <a title=\"1969&ndash;70 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1969%E2%80%9370_NBA_season\">1969&ndash;70 season</a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The Boston Celtics logo since 1968 features a <a title=\"Leprechaun\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leprechaun\">leprechaun</a> spinning a basketball, named Lucky, originally depicted with a large basketball for a background.<sup id=\"cite_ref-212\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-212\">[211]</a></sup> It was originally designed by Zang Auerbach, the brother of Celtics head coach <a title=\"Red Auerbach\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Auerbach\">Red Auerbach</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-CelticsLogo_3-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-CelticsLogo-3\">[3]</a></sup> Through the <a title=\"1995&ndash;96 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_NBA_season\">1995&ndash;96 season</a>, the logo's only colors were black, white and green.<sup id=\"cite_ref-213\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-213\">[212]</a></sup> Then for the <a title=\"1996&ndash;97 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_NBA_season\">1996&ndash;97 season</a>, celebrating the club's 50th anniversary, the logo got a full-color treatment. Lucky's face and hands were both painted tan, while gold was included on the vest, bow tie and hat, as well as brown on the ball and <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Shillelagh (club)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shillelagh_(club)\">shillelagh</a>, and black on its pants and shoes.<sup id=\"cite_ref-214\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-214\">[213]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Celtics also have various alternative logos, with the most popular being a white <a title=\"Shamrock\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shamrock\">shamrock</a> with the letters \"Celtics\" above it, wrapped in a green circle, which has been used since the <a title=\"1998&ndash;99 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_NBA_season\">1998&ndash;99 season</a>. The alternate logo is based on logos used by the Celtics before they used the Zang Auerbach leprechaun. For much of its history, the shamrock was trimmed in gold, as seen in the old team warmup jackets. A new secondary logo, unveiled in 2014, featured a variation of the leprechaun logo, in silhouette form.<sup id=\"cite_ref-215\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-215\">[214]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-LuckyAlternateLogo_216-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-LuckyAlternateLogo-216\">[215]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Uniforms\" class=\"mw-headline\">Uniforms</span></h3>\r\n<h4><span id=\"Primary_uniforms\" class=\"mw-headline\">Primary uniforms</span></h4>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tmulti tnone center\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner multiimageinner\" style=\"width: 792px; max-width: 792px;\">\r\n<div class=\"trow\">\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 222px; max-width: 222px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 275px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bill_Sharman,_Boston_Celtics,_signed.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bill_Sharman%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_signed.jpg/220px-Bill_Sharman%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_signed.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bill_Sharman%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_signed.jpg/330px-Bill_Sharman%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_signed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bill_Sharman%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_signed.jpg/440px-Bill_Sharman%2C_Boston_Celtics%2C_signed.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"220\" height=\"276\" data-file-width=\"1276\" data-file-height=\"1600\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 178px; max-width: 178px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 275px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dennis_Johnson_Lipofsky.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Dennis_Johnson_Lipofsky.jpg/176px-Dennis_Johnson_Lipofsky.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Dennis_Johnson_Lipofsky.jpg/264px-Dennis_Johnson_Lipofsky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Dennis_Johnson_Lipofsky.jpg/352px-Dennis_Johnson_Lipofsky.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"176\" height=\"276\" data-file-width=\"430\" data-file-height=\"674\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 186px; max-width: 186px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 275px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rajon_Rondo_Kyle_Singler_Will_Bynum.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Rajon_Rondo_Kyle_Singler_Will_Bynum.jpg/184px-Rajon_Rondo_Kyle_Singler_Will_Bynum.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Rajon_Rondo_Kyle_Singler_Will_Bynum.jpg/276px-Rajon_Rondo_Kyle_Singler_Will_Bynum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Rajon_Rondo_Kyle_Singler_Will_Bynum.jpg/368px-Rajon_Rondo_Kyle_Singler_Will_Bynum.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"184\" height=\"276\" data-file-width=\"667\" data-file-height=\"1000\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 198px; max-width: 198px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 275px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Semi_Ojeleye_(cropped).jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Semi_Ojeleye_%28cropped%29.jpg/196px-Semi_Ojeleye_%28cropped%29.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Semi_Ojeleye_%28cropped%29.jpg/294px-Semi_Ojeleye_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Semi_Ojeleye_%28cropped%29.jpg/392px-Semi_Ojeleye_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"196\" height=\"275\" data-file-width=\"1055\" data-file-height=\"1481\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"trow\" style=\"display: flex;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">The Celtics uniforms, as worn by <a title=\"Bill Sharman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Sharman\">Bill Sharman</a>, <a title=\"Dennis Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dennis_Johnson\">Dennis Johnson</a>, <a title=\"Rajon Rondo\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajon_Rondo\">Rajon Rondo</a> and <a title=\"Semi Ojeleye\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi_Ojeleye\">Semi Ojeleye</a>, have seen minimal changes since the 1950s.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>For much of their history, the Celtics wore green uniforms on the road and white uniforms at home. The basic template of the current Celtics' uniforms was formalized in the 1950s, and along the way they made a few adjustments in the lettering and stripes.</p>\r\n<p>Among the more notable changes in the uniforms were the switch from serifed to sans-serif block lettering in 1968, the addition of names in 1972, and the incorporation of the three-leaf shamrock logo in 1998. While the white uniforms remained largely intact, the green uniforms have featured either the city name (1950s&ndash;1965; 2014&ndash;present) or the team name (1965&ndash;2014).<sup id=\"cite_ref-217\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-217\">[216]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>When <a title=\"Nike, Inc.\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nike,_Inc.\">Nike</a> became the NBA's uniform provider in 2017, they decided to eliminate the \"home\" and \"away\" uniform designations. Thus the white Celtics uniforms became known as the \"Association\" uniforms while the green uniforms became the \"Icon\" uniforms. Both sets are now used regardless of home and road games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-218\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-218\">[217]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-219\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-219\">[218]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In January 2017, the Celtics signed a multi-year deal with <a title=\"General Electric\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Electric\">General Electric</a> where they became the \"exclusive Data and Analytics partner\" for the team. As part of the deal, GE agreed to pay the Celtics more than $7 million per year<sup id=\"cite_ref-220\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-220\">[219]</a></sup> to have the uniforms with a GE logo prominently placed on the left shoulder of jerseys in green and white. This was the first time a corporate logo were placed on the game uniforms.<sup id=\"cite_ref-CelticsGE_221-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-CelticsGE-221\">[220]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-222\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-222\">[221]</a></sup> Along with the GE logo, the Nike logo now emblazons the right shoulder of the Celtics' uniforms.</p>\r\n<p>In November 2020, the Celtics signed a multi-year deal with <a title=\"Vistaprint\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vistaprint\">Vistaprint</a> who became the main jersey sponsor of the team.<sup id=\"cite_ref-CelticsVistaprint_5-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-CelticsVistaprint-5\">[5]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h4><span id=\"Alternate_uniforms\" class=\"mw-headline\">Alternate uniforms</span></h4>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tmulti tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner multiimageinner\" style=\"width: 392px; max-width: 392px;\">\r\n<div class=\"trow\">\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 145px; max-width: 145px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 213px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ray_Allen_2008-01-13.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Ray_Allen_2008-01-13.jpg/143px-Ray_Allen_2008-01-13.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Ray_Allen_2008-01-13.jpg/215px-Ray_Allen_2008-01-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Ray_Allen_2008-01-13.jpg/286px-Ray_Allen_2008-01-13.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"143\" height=\"213\" data-file-width=\"2089\" data-file-height=\"3114\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 243px; max-width: 243px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 213px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Isaiah_Thomas_(32471151946).jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Isaiah_Thomas_%2832471151946%29.jpg/241px-Isaiah_Thomas_%2832471151946%29.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Isaiah_Thomas_%2832471151946%29.jpg/362px-Isaiah_Thomas_%2832471151946%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Isaiah_Thomas_%2832471151946%29.jpg/482px-Isaiah_Thomas_%2832471151946%29.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"241\" height=\"213\" data-file-width=\"3559\" data-file-height=\"3147\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"trow\" style=\"display: flex;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Ray Allen\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Allen\">Ray Allen</a> (left) wearing the alternate green uniform in 2008; <a title=\"Isaiah Thomas (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaiah_Thomas_(basketball)\">Isaiah Thomas</a> (right) wearing the alternate gray \"Parquet Pride\" uniform in 2017.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>From 2005 to 2017, the Celtics wore alternate green uniforms with black lettering and trim featuring the word \"Boston\" on the front side. One noticeable difference in the alternate uniforms was the black panels with a green shamrock, reminiscent of the original Celtics uniforms worn in the late 1940s.<sup id=\"cite_ref-223\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-223\">[222]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>A gray uniform set was also used from 2014 to 2017. Dubbed \"Parquet Pride\", the uniforms featured sleeves (a prominent figure in <a title=\"Adidas\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adidas\">Adidas</a>' NBA uniforms), white letters with green trim, the silhouetted leprechaun logo on the shorts, the shamrock logo on the left leg, and a parquet-like pattern on the sides.<sup id=\"cite_ref-224\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-224\">[223]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>For 2017 and beyond, the Celtics will wear black \"Statement\" uniforms (labeled by Nike in reference to the league's third jerseys). The uniform features a black base with \"Celtics\" in green lettering and white trim, and other than a few changes in the striping scheme, the uniform remained essentially the same. Starting in 2020, the \"Statement\" uniform would feature the <a title=\"Air Jordan\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_Jordan\">Air Jordan</a> brand logo, a feature previously exclusive to the <a title=\"Charlotte Hornets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets\">Charlotte Hornets</a> uniforms.<sup id=\"cite_ref-225\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-225\">[224]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h4><span id=\"Special_uniforms\" class=\"mw-headline\">Special uniforms</span></h4>\r\n<p>Between 2006 and 2017, the Celtics wore special <a title=\"Saint Patrick's Day in the United States\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Day_in_the_United_States#Basketball\">St. Patrick's Day</a> uniforms. The initial uniforms were worn from 2006 to 2013 and it strongly resembled their regular green uniforms save for gold and white trim and the city name in front.<sup id=\"cite_ref-226\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-226\">[225]</a></sup> For 2014 and 2015, the uniforms were sleeved, replaced the city name in front in favor of the team name, and now resembled their green/black alternates.<sup id=\"cite_ref-227\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-227\">[226]</a></sup> In 2016 and 2017, the uniforms were again sleeveless and featured the city name in front, but kept the previous striping.</p>\r\n<p>During the <a title=\"2007 NBA Europe Live Tour\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2007_NBA_Europe_Live_Tour\">NBA Europe Live Tour</a> prior to the <a title=\"2007&ndash;08 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_NBA_season\">2007&ndash;08 season</a>, the Celtics used the alternate road jerseys in their game against the <a title=\"Toronto Raptors\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toronto_Raptors\">Toronto Raptors</a> in Rome, except that the words \"Boston\" on the front side of the jersey and the shamrock on the shorts and on the reverse side of the jersey contained the green, white and red <a title=\"Flag of Italy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_Italy\">tricolors</a> of the <a title=\"Flag of Italy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_Italy\">Italian flag</a>. In the second game in London, the regular road jerseys featured a patch containing the <a title=\"Union Jack\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_Jack\">Union Jack</a>.</p>\r\n<p>At the <a title=\"2008&ndash;09 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_NBA_season\">2008&ndash;09 season</a> opener against the Cleveland Cavaliers, the Celtics wore a modified version of their home uniforms, accented with gold, to commemorate last season's championship team.</p>\r\n<p>The Celtics have also worn special edition <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"National Basketball Association Christmas games\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association_Christmas_games\">Christmas Day</a> uniforms since the 2008&ndash;09 season. For the first four games, they wore their regular green uniforms modified with the NBA logo inside a <a title=\"Snowflake\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snowflake\">snowflake</a>. Then in the <a title=\"2012&ndash;13 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_NBA_season\">2012&ndash;13 season</a>, they wore monochrome uniforms with green lettering trimmed in white. For the <a title=\"2016&ndash;17 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_NBA_season\">2016&ndash;17 season</a>, the Celtics wore a special green uniform with a more ornate script lettering, but without the additional striping.</p>\r\n<p>Starting with the 2017&ndash;18 season, the Celtics wore special edition \"City\" uniforms designed by Nike. Their first \"City\" uniforms were in gray and featured a pattern of the parquet floor throughout, a green shamrock with white trim on the left leg, green letters with white trim, Red Auerbach's signature near the uniform tag, and a portion of the 2008 championship banner on the beltline.<sup id=\"cite_ref-228\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-228\">[227]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>For the 2018&ndash;19 season, the Celtics wore white \"City\" uniforms with green letters and shamrocks trimmed in gold. It also has Red Auerbach's signature near the uniform tag and a gold-trimmed alternate Celtics logo on the beltline.<sup id=\"cite_ref-229\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-229\">[228]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-230\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-230\">[229]</a></sup> In addition, the Celtics wore an \"Earned\" edition uniform exclusive only to the 16 teams that made the <a title=\"2018 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_NBA_playoffs\">2018 NBA playoffs</a>. Their rendition is a palette swap of the \"City\" uniforms with a green base and gold letters and shamrocks with white trim.<sup id=\"cite_ref-231\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-231\">[230]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Celtics' \"City\" uniform for the 2019&ndash;20 season featured a green base and a stylized \"Boston\" wordmark and numbers in gold with black trim. A <a title=\"Celtic knot\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtic_knot\">Celtic knot</a> in the shape of a shamrock adorn the beltline.<sup id=\"cite_ref-232\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-232\">[231]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The 2020&ndash;21 Celtics' \"City\" uniform was patterned after the 17 championship banners that adorn the TD Garden rafters. The uniform, which is white with thick green stripes, features the full name in <a title=\"Futura (typeface)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Futura_(typeface)\">Futura Condensed</a> stacked in front, and Red Auerbach's signature and quote \"The Boston Celtics are not a basketball team. They're a way of life.\" appears above the manufacturer's tag.<sup id=\"cite_ref-233\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-233\">[232]</a></sup> The Celtics also released a second \"Earned\" uniform after qualifying in the <a title=\"2020 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_NBA_playoffs\">2020 NBA playoffs</a>; this design features a dark green base with Celtic and lime green striping, and the letters were rendered in Celtic green with white trim.<sup id=\"cite_ref-234\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-234\">[233]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Celtics' green \"City\" uniform for the 2021&ndash;22 season was a mix of previous uniform designs. The neck and arm striping was taken from their current uniforms. The green lettering with white drop shadows was a nod to the 1949 uniform design. The gray triangles on the shorts represented the franchise's initial uniforms; the left side contained the team's 75th anniversary emblem, while the right side contained a green-and-white version of the Red Auerbach memorial shamrock used in the 2006&ndash;07 season. Contrasting nameplates on the back were inspired by the warmup jackets the team used for much of its history, and the original \"jumping leprechaun\" logo from the 1960s was added to the waist. Retired numbers, the Auerbach signature and quotation (see 2021 \"City\" uniform), and 17 shamrocks representing each championship season, surrounded the jock tag.<sup id=\"cite_ref-235\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-235\">[234]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The 2022&ndash;23 \"City\" uniform served as a memorial to Bill Russell, who died on July 31. The uniform is dark green with metallic gold and black accents, and has the \"Celtics\" wordmark inspired by the Slade's Bar &amp; Grill restaurant once owned by Russell. The black stripes contained 11 gold diamonds on each side, commemorating each of Russell's championships, and also featured a grayscale pattern of the parquet floor. The waistband contained Russell's jersey no. 6 surrounded by the 11 gold diamonds.<sup id=\"cite_ref-236\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-236\">[235]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h4><span id=\"Memorial_patches\" class=\"mw-headline\">Memorial patches</span></h4>\r\n<p>During the <a title=\"2006&ndash;07 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NBA_season\">2006&ndash;07 season</a>, the Celtics wore a commemorative patch of a black <a title=\"Shamrock\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shamrock\">shamrock</a> with the nickname \"Red\" in green letters on the right top of the jersey in remembrance of <a title=\"Red Auerbach\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Auerbach\">Red Auerbach</a>, who died shortly prior to the beginning of the season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-jerseyhonors_237-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-jerseyhonors-237\">[236]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The team has honored deceased members of the Celtics family with a commemorative black band on the left shoulder strap of the jersey. It has been featured ten times to date: <a title=\"Walter A. Brown\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_A._Brown\">Walter Brown</a> (<a title=\"1964&ndash;65 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1964%E2%80%9365_NBA_season\">1964&ndash;65</a>), <a title=\"Robert Schmertz\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Schmertz\">Bob Schmertz</a> (<a title=\"1975&ndash;76 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1975%E2%80%9376_NBA_season\">1975&ndash;76</a>), Joan Cohen (<a title=\"1989&ndash;90 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_NBA_season\">1989&ndash;90</a>), <a title=\"Johnny Most\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johnny_Most\">Johnny Most</a> and <a title=\"Reggie Lewis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reggie_Lewis\">Reggie Lewis</a> (<a title=\"1993&ndash;94 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_NBA_season\">1993&ndash;94</a>), Dorothy Auerbach (<a title=\"2000&ndash;01 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_NBA_season\">2000&ndash;01</a>), <a title=\"Dennis Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dennis_Johnson\">Dennis Johnson</a> (<a title=\"2006&ndash;07 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NBA_season\">2006&ndash;07</a>),<sup id=\"cite_ref-jerseyhonors_237-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-jerseyhonors-237\">[236]</a></sup> <a title=\"Jim Loscutoff\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Loscutoff\">Jim Loscutoff</a> (<a title=\"2015&ndash;16 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_NBA_season\">2015&ndash;16</a>), <a title=\"Jo Jo White\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jo_Jo_White\">Jo Jo White</a> (<a title=\"2017&ndash;18 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_NBA_season\">2017&ndash;18</a>), <a title=\"John Havlicek\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Havlicek\">John Havlicek</a> (<a title=\"2018&ndash;19 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_NBA_season\">2018&ndash;19</a>), <a title=\"Tom Heinsohn\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Heinsohn\">Tom Heinsohn</a>, and <a title=\"K. C. Jones\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K._C._Jones\">K. C. Jones</a> (both <a title=\"2020&ndash;21 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_NBA_season\">2020&ndash;21</a>). During the <a title=\"2019&ndash;20 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_NBA_season\">2019&ndash;20 season</a>, the Celtics wore a black band in honor of two people who had never been part of the Celtics organization; former NBA commissioner <a title=\"David Stern\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Stern\">David Stern</a> and former <a title=\"Los Angeles Lakers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers\">Los Angeles Lakers</a> star <a title=\"Kobe Bryant\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kobe_Bryant\">Kobe Bryant</a>. The Celtics have also worn a black band for reasons not directly related to the franchise, such as the <a title=\"Boston Marathon bombing\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Marathon_bombing\">Boston Marathon bombing</a> in 2013, and the death of <a title=\"Isaiah Thomas (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaiah_Thomas_(basketball)\">Isaiah Thomas</a>' younger sister during the <a title=\"2017 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_NBA_playoffs\">2017 NBA playoffs</a>.</p>\r\n<p>In the <a title=\"2022&ndash;23 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022%E2%80%9323_NBA_season\">2022&ndash;23 season</a>, the Celtics joined the rest of the NBA in wearing the black no. 6 patch in memory of <a title=\"Bill Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Russell\">Bill Russell</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-238\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-238\">[237]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h4><span id=\"Uniform_traditions\" class=\"mw-headline\">Uniform traditions</span></h4>\r\n<p>The team also had the tradition of wearing black sneakers through most of their history. According to legend, Celtics patriarch <a title=\"Red Auerbach\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Auerbach\">Red Auerbach</a> had a problem with the white sneakers, claiming that the white sneakers can easily get dirty; hence starting a long tradition with the black sneakers. In the early 1970s, the Celtics changed their sneaker color to green, but by 1985, returned to the customary black due to the difficulty of producing the right shade of Celtic green.<sup id=\"cite_ref-ctwrblk_239-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-ctwrblk-239\">[238]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Prior to the <a title=\"2003&ndash;04 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_NBA_season\">2003&ndash;04 season</a>, current Celtics general manager <a title=\"Danny Ainge\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danny_Ainge\">Danny Ainge</a> and captain <a title=\"Paul Pierce\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Pierce\">Paul Pierce</a> suggested wearing white sneakers, in due part to a growing number of teams wearing black sneakers. Auerbach gladly accepted and the white sneakers have remained since on home games. They still wore the black sneakers on away games, but in the <a title=\"2008&ndash;09 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_NBA_season\">2008&ndash;09 season</a>, they wore white sneakers with green and gold accents while wearing their St. Patrick's Day jerseys on the road. Most recently, when the Celtics play on <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"National Basketball Association Christmas games\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association_Christmas_games\">Christmas Day</a>, they wore white or green sneakers with red and gold accents.<sup id=\"cite_ref-240\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-240\">[239]</a></sup> Since the 2009&ndash;10 season, the NBA relaxed its rules on specified sneaker colors, and Celtics players are now seen wearing custom-made and personalized sneakers at home and on the road, although for the most part they wear either green, white or black sneakers.</p>\r\n<p>The Celtics were the only team to wear warmup jackets with the player names on the back. During the 1980s, this style was dominant in most NBA warmup jackets, but by the late 1990s, this style gradually declined. The Celtics, however, kept the design in keeping with tradition, before discontinuing the practice after the 2011&ndash;12 season in favor of a templated jacket design common to all 30 teams.</p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Television_and_radio\" class=\"mw-headline\">Television and radio</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"List of Boston Celtics broadcasters\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Boston_Celtics_broadcasters\">List of Boston Celtics broadcasters</a></div>\r\n<p><a title=\"NBC Sports Boston\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC_Sports_Boston\">NBC Sports Boston</a> is the Boston Celtics' main television outlet, having aired its games since 1981 when the station was known as PRISM New England. In 1983, it rebranded as SportsChannel New England. Like all the other SportsChannel networks, the New England channel was rebranded as <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Fox Sports Net\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fox_Sports_Net\">Fox Sports</a> New England when former owner <a title=\"Cablevision\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cablevision\">Cablevision</a> entered into a partnership with <a title=\"Liberty Media\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberty_Media\">Liberty Media</a> and <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"News Corporation (1980&ndash;2013)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/News_Corporation_(1980%E2%80%932013)\">News Corporation</a> in 1998. Comcast purchased Cablevision's original network stake in 2001, then acquired the remaining stake in what was now <a title=\"Fox Sports Networks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fox_Sports_Networks\">FSN</a> New England in 2007 and rebranded the network as Comcast SportsNet New England. In 2017, all CSN networks (including CSN New England) were renamed as <a title=\"NBC Sports Regional Networks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC_Sports_Regional_Networks\">NBC Sports Regional Networks</a> in reference to Comcast's current ownership of <a title=\"NBCUniversal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBCUniversal\">NBCUniversal</a>.</p>\r\n<p><a title=\"Mike Gorman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Gorman\">Mike Gorman</a> provides the play-by-play with former Celtics player <a title=\"Brian Scalabrine\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Scalabrine\">Brian Scalabrine</a> serving as analyst.</p>\r\n<p>All Celtics games are heard on radio through <a title=\"Beasley Broadcast Group\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beasley_Broadcast_Group\">Beasley Broadcast Group</a>'s <a title=\"WBZ-FM\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WBZ-FM\">WBZ-FM</a> (98.5, otherwise branded as \"The Sports Hub\"), with play-by-play from <a title=\"Sean Grande\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sean_Grande\">Sean Grande</a> and color commentary from <a title=\"Cedric Maxwell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cedric_Maxwell\">Cedric Maxwell</a>, a deal in place since the 2013&ndash;14 season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-241\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics#cite_note-241\">[240]</a></sup> It is carried on stations in 5 of the 6 New England States via the <a title=\"Boston Celtics Radio Network\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics_Radio_Network\">Boston Celtics Radio Network</a>.</p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Management\" class=\"mw-headline\">Management</span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Ownership_history\" class=\"mw-headline\">Ownership history</span></h3>\r\n<table class=\"wikitable\" style=\"text-align: center;\">\r\n<tbody>\r\n<tr>\r\n<th style=\"background-color: #008348; id=\"cite_note-2017_draft_lottery-134\"></li>\r\n</ol>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"reflist\">\r\n<div class=\"mw-references-wrap\">\r\n<ol class=\"references\">\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-2017_draft_lottery-134\"><span class=\"reference-text\">This pick originally belonged to the <a title=\"Brooklyn Nets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets\">Brooklyn Nets</a>, but was sent to the Celtics in the 2013 trade involving Paul Pierce and Kevin Garnett. The Nets had the worst record in the previous season, which gave the Celtics the highest chance of winning the lottery.</span></li>\r\n</ol>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<h2><span id=\"References\" class=\"mw-headline\">References</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"reflist\">\r\n<div class=\"mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns\">\r\n<ol class=\"references\">\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-1\"></li>\r\n</ol>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<ul>\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-1\"><span class=\"reference-text\"><cite class=\"citation web cs1\"><a class=\"external text\" href=\"https://www.nba.com/stats/team/1610612738/seasons\" rel=\"nofollow\">\"NBA.com/Stats&ndash;Boston Celtics seasons\"</a>. <em>Stats.NBA.com</em>.
